style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="color: #202122; background:lavender">Personal details</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Born</th><td <div class="marriage-display-inline"><div style="display:inline-block;line-height:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Emilie_Schenkl" title="Emilie Schenkl">Emilie Schenkl</a></div>&#32;<div style="display:inline-block;">&#8203;</div>&#40;<abbr title="married">m.</abbr>&#160;1937&#41;<wbr />&#8203;</div><sup id="cite&#95;ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>c<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Children</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Anita_Bose_Pfaff" title="Anita Bose Pfaff">Anita Bose Pfaff</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Parents</th><td class="infobox-data"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1126788409">.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}</style><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Janakinath_Bose" title="Janakinath Bose">Janakinath Bose</a> (father)</li><li><a February 1916<sup id="cite&#95;ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>d<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>e<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li><li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Church_College" title="Scottish Church College">Scottish Church College</a>, Calcutta, 20 July 1917–1919</li><li><a href="/wiki/Fitzwilliam_College,_Cambridge#History" title="Fitzwilliam College, Cambridge">Fitzwilliam Hall</a>, class="infobox-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409" /><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Calcutta" title="University of scope="row" class="infobox-label">Signature</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="skin-invert notpageimage" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:S_Basu.png" class="mw-file-description" title="Subhas Chandra Bose&#39;s signature"><img alt="Signature of Subhas Chandra Bose in English and Bengali" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/S_Basu.png/207px-S_Basu.png" decoding="async" width="128" height="45" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ee/S_Basu.png 2x" data-file-width="207" data-file-height="72" /></a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-below" style="border-top: 1px solid right;"><div></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Subhas Chandra Bose</b><sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>g<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> (23 January 1897&#160;– 18 August 1945) was an Indian <a href="/wiki/Nationalism#Anti-colonial" title="Nationalism">anti-colonial nationalist</a> whose defiance of <a href="/wiki/British_raj" class="mw-redirect" title="British raj">British authority in India</a> made him a hero among many Indians,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Mythic&#95;21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mythic-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>h<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>i<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>j<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but his wartime alliances with <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Fascism" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Fascism">Fascist Japan</a> left a legacy vexed by <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarianism</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lal-gandhi-inc-jewish-question1&#95;26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lal-gandhi-inc-jewish-question1-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>k<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>l<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>m<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anti-Semitism" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Semitism">anti-Semitism</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lal-gandhi-inc-jewish-question2&#95;32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lal-gandhi-inc-jewish-question2-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-disturbing&#95;33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-disturbing-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>n<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>o<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>p<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>q<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>r<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-cronin-2025&#95;42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cronin-2025-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Military_incompetence" title="Military incompetence">military failure</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>s<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-gordonunrealistic&#95;46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gordonunrealistic-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-combined-military-lead&#95;47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-combined-military-lead-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>t<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>u<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The honorific 'Netaji' (<a href="/wiki/Hindustani_language" title="Hindustani language">Hindustani</a>: "Respected Leader") was first applied to Bose in Germany in early 1942—by the Indian soldiers of the <i><a href="/wiki/Indian_Legion" title="Indian Legion">Indische Legion</a></i> and by the German and Indian officials in the <a href="/wiki/Special_Bureau_for_India" title="Special Bureau for India">Special Bureau for India</a> in Berlin. It is now used throughout India.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>v<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990459–460&#95;53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990459–460-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Bose was born into wealth and privilege in a large <a href="/wiki/Bengalis" title="Bengalis">Bengali</a> family in <a href="/wiki/Orissa" class="mw-redirect" title="Orissa">Orissa</a> during the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a>. The early recipient of an <a href="/wiki/Anglocentrism" title="Anglocentrism">Anglo-centric</a> education, he was sent after college to England to take the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Civil_Service" title="Indian Civil Service">Indian Civil Service</a> examination. He succeeded with distinction in the vital first exam but demurred at taking the routine final exam, citing nationalism to be the higher calling. Returning to India in 1921, Bose joined the <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">nationalist movement</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a>. He followed <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru" title="Jawaharlal Nehru">Jawaharlal Nehru</a> to leadership in a group within the Congress which was less keen on constitutional reform and more open to socialism.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>w<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bose became Congress president in 1938. After reelection in 1939, differences arose between him and the Congress leaders, including Gandhi, over the future federation of <a href="/wiki/British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="British India">British India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Princely_state" title="Princely state">princely states</a>, but also because discomfort had grown among the Congress leadership over Bose's negotiable attitude to non-violence, and his plans for greater powers for himself.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-matthews-bose-congress&#95;56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-matthews-bose-congress-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After the large majority of the <a href="/wiki/Congress_Working_Committee" title="Congress Working Committee">Congress Working Committee</a> members resigned in protest,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-haithcox-bose-andINC-oldguard&#95;57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haithcox-bose-andINC-oldguard-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bose resigned as president and was eventually ousted from the party.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELow2002297,&#95;313&#95;58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELow2002297,_313-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990420–428&#95;59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990420–428-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 1941 Bose arrived in Nazi Germany, where the leadership offered unexpected but equivocal sympathy for India's independence.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes201165–67,&#95;152&#95;60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes201165–67,_152-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> German funds were employed to open a Free India Centre in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>. A 3,000-strong <a href="/wiki/Free_India_Legion" class="mw-redirect" title="Free India Legion">Free India Legion</a> was recruited from among Indian POWs captured by <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Rommel" title="Erwin Rommel">Erwin Rommel</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Afrika_Korps" title="Afrika Korps">Afrika Korps</a> to serve under Bose.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes201176&#95;61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes201176-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>x<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Although peripheral to their main goals, the Germans inconclusively considered a land invasion of India throughout 1941. By the spring of 1942, the German army was <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)#Don,_Volga,_and_Caucasus:_Summer_1942" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">mired in Russia</a> and Bose became keen to move to southeast Asia, where Japan had just won quick victories.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes201187–88&#95;64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes201187–88-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> during his only meeting with Bose in late May 1942 agreed to arrange a submarine.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes2011114–116&#95;65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes2011114–116-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During this time, Bose became a father; his wife,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes201115&#95;8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes201115-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>y<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or companion,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990344–345&#95;67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990344–345-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>z<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Emilie_Schenkl" title="Emilie Schenkl">Emilie Schenkl</a>, gave birth to <a href="/wiki/Anita_Bose_Pfaff" title="Anita Bose Pfaff">a baby girl</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes201115,&#95;65–67&#95;69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes201115,_65–67-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Identifying strongly with the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a>, Bose boarded a German submarine in February 1943.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes2011141–143&#95;70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes2011141–143-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBose2005255&#95;71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBose2005255-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Off Madagascar, he was transferred to a Japanese submarine from which he disembarked in <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_the_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Japanese occupation of the Dutch East Indies">Japanese-held Sumatra</a> in May 1943.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes2011141–143&#95;70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes2011141–143-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>With Japanese support, Bose revamped the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Army" title="Indian National Army">Indian National Army</a> (INA), which comprised Indian <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">prisoners of war</a> of the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_army" class="mw-redirect" title="British Indian army">British Indian army</a> who had been captured by the Japanese in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Singapore" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Singapore">Battle of Singapore</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008avii–ix,&#95;xvi–xvii,&#95;210–212&#95;72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008avii–ix,_xvi–xvii,_210–212-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-gordon-ijss-ina&#95;73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gordon-ijss-ina-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Azad_Hind" title="Azad Hind">Provisional Government of Free India</a> (Azad Hind) was declared on the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_the_Andaman_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese occupation of the Andaman Islands">Japanese-occupied</a> <a href="/wiki/Andaman_and_Nicobar_Islands" title="Andaman and Nicobar Islands">Andaman and Nicobar Islands</a> and was nominally presided over by Bose.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELow199331–32&#95;74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELow199331–32-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEWolpert2000339&#95;2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolpert2000339-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>aa<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Although Bose was unusually driven and charismatic, the Japanese considered him to be militarily unskilled,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-gordonunrealistic&#95;46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gordonunrealistic-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and his soldierly effort was short-lived. In late 1944 and early 1945, the British Indian Army reversed the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Operation_U-Go" title="Operation U-Go">attack on India</a>. Almost half of the Japanese forces and fully half of the participating INA contingent were killed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>ab<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The remaining INA was driven down the Malay Peninsula and surrendered with the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Tiderace" title="Operation Tiderace">recapture of Singapore</a>. Bose chose to escape to Manchuria to seek a future in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> which he believed to have turned anti-British.
</p><p>Bose <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Subhas_Chandra_Bose" title="Death of Subhas Chandra Bose">died from third-degree burns after his plane crashed</a> in Taiwan (then under <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_under_Japanese_rule" title="Taiwan under Japanese rule">Japanese occupation</a>) on 18 August 1945.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>ac<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some Indians did not believe that the crash had occurred,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>ad<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> expecting Bose to return to secure India's independence.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>ae<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>af<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>ag<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Indian National Congress, the main instrument of Indian nationalism, praised Bose's patriotism but distanced itself from his tactics and ideology.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200721&#95;87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200721-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The British Raj, never seriously threatened by the INA, charged 300 INA officers with treason in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Army_trials" title="Indian National Army trials">Indian National Army trials</a>, but eventually backtracked in the face of opposition by the Congress,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>ah<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and a new mood in Britain for rapid decolonisation in India.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200721&#95;87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200721-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMetcalfMetcalf2012210&#95;20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMetcalfMetcalf2012210-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bose's legacy is mixed. Among many in India, he is seen as a hero, his saga serving as a would-be counterpoise to the many actions of regeneration, negotiation, and reconciliation over a quarter-century through which the independence of India was achieved.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>ai<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many on the right and far-right often venerate him as a champion of Indian nationalism as well as Hindu identity by spreading conspiracy theories.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  His collaborations with <a href="/wiki/Statism_in_Sh%C5%8Dwa_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Statism in Shōwa Japan">Japanese fascism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a> pose serious ethical dilemmas,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-disturbing&#95;33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-disturbing-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>n<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> especially his reluctance to publicly criticise the worst excesses of German anti-Semitism from 1938 onwards or to offer refuge in India to its victims.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Biography">Biography</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="1897–1921:_Early_life"><span id="1897.E2.80.931921:_Early_life"></span>1897–1921: Early life</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Joppen1907BritishBengalBritishBurmaA.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8b/Joppen1907BritishBengalBritishBurmaA.jpg/250px-Joppen1907BritishBengalBritishBurmaA.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="342" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8b/Joppen1907BritishBengalBritishBurmaA.jpg/500px-Joppen1907BritishBengalBritishBurmaA.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="877" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption><b>Map 1</b>: The growth of <a href="/wiki/Bengal_presidency" class="mw-redirect" title="Bengal presidency">British Bengal</a> between 1757 and 1803 is shown in shades of brown. Cuttack is approximately 225 miles (362&#160;km) southwest of Calcutta.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Subhas Chandra Bose was born to Bengali parents <a href="/wiki/Prabhabati_Bose" title="Prabhabati Bose">Prabhabati Bose</a> (<span title="Name at birth"><a href="/wiki/Birth_name#Maiden_and_married_names" title="Birth name">née</a>&#160;Dutt</span>) and <a href="/wiki/Janakinath_Bose" title="Janakinath Bose">Janakinath Bose</a> on 23 January 1897 in <a href="/wiki/Cuttack" title="Cuttack">Cuttack</a>—in what is today the state of <a href="/wiki/Odisha" title="Odisha">Odisha</a> in India but was part of the <a href="/wiki/Bengal_Presidency" title="Bengal Presidency">Bengal Presidency</a> in <a href="/wiki/British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="British India">British India</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>aj<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>ak<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Prabhabati, or familiarly <i>Mā jananī</i> (<abbr style="font-size:85%" title="literal translation">lit.</abbr><span style="white-space: nowrap;">&#8201;</span><span class="gloss-quot">'</span><span class="gloss-text">mother</span><span class="gloss-quot">'</span>), the anchor of family life, had her first child at age 14 and 13 children thereafter. Subhas was the ninth child and the sixth son.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon19909,&#95;14&#95;101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon19909,_14-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Jankinath, a successful lawyer and government <a href="/wiki/Advocate" title="Advocate">pleader</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes20111&#95;99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes20111-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> was loyal to the government of <a href="/wiki/British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="British India">British India</a> and scrupulous about matters of language and the law. A self-made man from the rural outskirts of <a href="/wiki/Calcutta" class="mw-redirect" title="Calcutta">Calcutta</a>, he had remained in touch with his roots, returning annually to his village during the <i><a href="/wiki/Durga_Puja" title="Durga Puja">pooja</a></i> holidays.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199012,&#95;13&#95;102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199012,_13-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Following his five older brothers, Bose entered the Baptist Mission's Protestant European School in <a href="/wiki/Cuttack" title="Cuttack">Cuttack</a> in January 1902.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199032&#95;10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199032-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> English was the medium of all instruction in the school, the majority of the students being European or <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Indians" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Indians">Anglo-Indians</a> of mixed British and Indian ancestry.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a102–103&#95;97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a102–103-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The curriculum included English—correctly written and spoken—Latin, the Bible, good manners, British geography, and British History; no Indian languages were taught.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a102–103&#95;97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a102–103-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199032&#95;10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199032-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The choice of the school was Bose's father's, who wanted his sons to speak flawless English with flawless intonation, believing both to be important for access to the British in India.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199011&#95;103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199011-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The school contrasted with Subhas's home, where only <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a> was spoken. At home, his mother worshipped the <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> goddesses <a href="/wiki/Durga" title="Durga">Durga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kali" title="Kali">Kali</a>, told stories from the epics <a href="/wiki/Mahabharata" title="Mahabharata">Mahabharata</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ramayana" title="Ramayana">Ramayana</a>, and sang Bengali religious songs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199032&#95;10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199032-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> From her, Subhas imbibed a nurturing spirit, looking for situations in which to help people in distress, preferring gardening around the house to joining in sports with other boys.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199033&#95;11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199033-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His father, who was reserved in manner and busy with professional life, was a distant presence in a large family, causing Subhas to feel he had a nondescript childhood.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199031–32&#95;104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199031–32-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Still, Janakinath read <a href="/wiki/English_literature" title="English literature">English literature</a> avidly—<a href="/wiki/John_Milton" title="John Milton">John Milton</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Cowper" title="William Cowper">William Cowper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Arnold" title="Matthew Arnold">Matthew Arnold</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare" class="mw-redirect" title="Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Hamlet" title="Hamlet">Hamlet</a></i> being among his favourites; several of his sons were to become English literature enthusiasts like him.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199011&#95;103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199011-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Subhas_Bose_standing_extreme_right_with_his_large_family_Cuttack,_India_1905.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Subhas_Bose_standing_extreme_right_with_his_large_family_Cuttack%2C_India_1905.jpg/250px-Subhas_Bose_standing_extreme_right_with_his_large_family_Cuttack%2C_India_1905.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="176" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Subhas_Bose_standing_extreme_right_with_his_large_family_Cuttack%2C_India_1905.jpg/500px-Subhas_Bose_standing_extreme_right_with_his_large_family_Cuttack%2C_India_1905.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="749" data-file-height="526" /></a><figcaption>Janakinath Bose, Prabhabati Bose, and their family, ca. 1905. <a href="/wiki/Sarat_Chandra_Bose" title="Sarat Chandra Bose">Sarat Chandra Bose</a> (standing, centre) and Subhas Bose (aged 8, standing, extreme right).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990150&#95;105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990150-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1909, the 12-year-old Subhas Bose followed his five brothers to the <a href="/wiki/Ravenshaw_Collegiate_School" title="Ravenshaw Collegiate School">Ravenshaw Collegiate School</a> in Cuttack.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199033&#95;11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199033-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Here, Bengali and <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> were also taught, as were ideas from Hindu scriptures such as the <a href="/wiki/Vedas" title="Vedas">Vedas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Upanishads" title="Upanishads">Upanishads</a> not usually picked up at home.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199033&#95;11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199033-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Although his Western education continued apace, he began to wear Indian clothes and engage in religious speculation. To his mother, he wrote long letters which displayed acquaintance with the ideas of the Bengali mystic <a href="/wiki/Ramakrishna_Paramahamsa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ramakrishna Paramahamsa">Ramakrishna Paramahamsa</a> and his disciple <a href="/wiki/Swami_Vivekananda" title="Swami Vivekananda">Swami Vivekananda</a>, and the novel <i><a href="/wiki/Ananda_Math" class="mw-redirect" title="Ananda Math">Ananda Math</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Bankim_Chandra_Chatterjee" title="Bankim Chandra Chatterjee">Bankim Chandra Chatterjee</a>, popular then among young Hindu men.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199034–35&#95;106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199034–35-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Despite the preoccupation, Subhas was able to demonstrate an ability when needed to focus on his studies, to compete, and to succeed in exams. In 1912, he secured the second position in the matriculation examination conducted under the auspices of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Calcutta" title="University of Calcutta">University of Calcutta</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199019,&#95;37&#95;107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199019,_37-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Subhas Bose followed his five brothers again in 1913 to <a href="/wiki/Presidency_College,_Kolkata" class="mw-redirect" title="Presidency College, Kolkata">Presidency College, Calcutta</a>, the historic and traditional college for Bengal's upper-<a href="/wiki/Caste" title="Caste">caste</a> Hindu men.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199019,&#95;37&#95;107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199019,_37-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199020&#95;108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199020-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He chose to study philosophy, his readings including <a href="/wiki/Immanuel_Kant" title="Immanuel Kant">Kant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georg_Wilhelm_Friedrich_Hegel" title="Georg Wilhelm Friedrich Hegel">Hegel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henri_Bergson" title="Henri Bergson">Bergson</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Western_philosophy" title="Western philosophy">Western philosophers</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199037&#95;109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199037-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A year earlier, he had befriended <a href="/wiki/Hemanta_Kumar_Sarkar" title="Hemanta Kumar Sarkar">Hemanta Kumar Sarkar</a>, a confidant and partner in religious yearnings.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199042–43&#95;110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199042–43-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At Presidency, their emotional ties grew stronger.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199042–43&#95;110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199042–43-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the fanciful language of religious imagery, they declared their pure love for each other.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199042–43&#95;110-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199042–43-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the long vacations of 1914, they traveled to northern India for several months to search for a spiritual <a href="/wiki/Guru" title="Guru">guru</a> to guide them.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199042–43&#95;110-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199042–43-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Subhas's family was not told clearly about the trip, leading them to think he had run away. During the trip, in which the guru proved elusive, Subhas came down with typhoid fever.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199042–43&#95;110-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199042–43-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His absence caused emotional distress to his parents, leading both parents to break down upon his return.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199042–43&#95;110-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199042–43-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Heated words were exchanged between <a href="/wiki/Janakinath_Bose" title="Janakinath Bose">Janakinath</a> and Subhas. It took the return of Subhas's favorite brother, <a href="/wiki/Sarat_Chandra_Bose" title="Sarat Chandra Bose">Sarat Chandra Bose</a>, from law studies in England for the tempers to subside. Subhas returned to presidency and busied himself with studies, debating and student journalism.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199042–43&#95;110-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199042–43-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In February 1916, Bose was alleged to have masterminded,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes20111&#95;99-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes20111-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or participated in, an incident involving E. F. Oaten, Professor of History at Presidency.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199048&#95;12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199048-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Before the incident, it was claimed by the students, Oaten had made rude remarks about Indian culture, and collared and pushed some students; according to Oaten, the students were making an unacceptably loud noise just outside his class.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199048&#95;12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199048-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A few days later, on 15 February, some students accosted Oaten on a stairway, surrounded him, beat him with sandals, and took to flight.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199048&#95;12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199048-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> An inquiry committee was constituted. Although Oaten, who was unhurt, could not identify his assailants, a college servant testified to seeing Subhas Bose and his classmate <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ananga_Mohan_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ananga Mohan Dam (page does not exist)">Ananga Dam</a> among those fleeing, confirming for the authorities what they had determined to be the rumour among the students.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199048&#95;12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199048-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Both Bose and Ananga Dam<sup id="cite&#95;ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> were expelled from the college and rusticated from the University of Calcutta.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199049&#95;112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199049-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The incident shocked Calcutta and caused anguish to Bose's family.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes20111&#95;99-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes20111-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He was ordered back to Cuttack. His family's connections were employed to pressure <a href="/wiki/Asutosh_Mukherjee" class="mw-redirect" title="Asutosh Mukherjee">Asutosh Mukherjee</a>, the Vice-Chancellor of Calcutta University.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199049&#95;112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199049-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Despite this, Subhas Bose's expulsion remained in place until 20 July 1917, when the Syndicate of Calcutta University granted him permission to return, but to another college.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199052&#95;13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199052-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He joined <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Church_College,_Calcutta" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Church College, Calcutta">Scottish Church College</a>, receiving his B.A. in 1918 in the <a href="/wiki/British_undergraduate_degree_classification#First-class_honours" title="British undergraduate degree classification">First Class</a> with honours in philosophy, placing second among all philosophy students in Calcutta University.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199054&#95;113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199054-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Hindu_college_calcutta1851.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3c/Hindu_college_calcutta1851.jpg/250px-Hindu_college_calcutta1851.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="196" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3c/Hindu_college_calcutta1851.jpg/500px-Hindu_college_calcutta1851.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="712" data-file-height="558" /></a><figcaption>A photograph (1851) of <a href="/wiki/Presidency_College,_Kolkata" class="mw-redirect" title="Presidency College, Kolkata">Presidency College</a>, Calcutta which Subhas Bose entered in 1913, but from which he was expelled in 1916</figcaption></figure>
<p>At his father's urging, Subhas Bose agreed to travel to England to prepare and appear for the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Civil_Service_(British_India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Civil Service (British India)">Indian Civil Services</a> (ICS) examination.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199055&#95;114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199055-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Arriving in London on 20 October 1919, Subhas readied his application for the ICS.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199055–56&#95;115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199055–56-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For his references he put down <a href="/wiki/Satyendra_Prasanna_Sinha,_1st_Baron_Sinha" title="Satyendra Prasanna Sinha, 1st Baron Sinha">Lord Sinha of Raipur</a>, Under Secretary of State for India, and <a href="/wiki/Bhupendra_Nath_Bose" title="Bhupendra Nath Bose">Bhupendranath Basu</a>, a wealthy Calcutta lawyer who sat on the Council of India in London.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199055&#95;114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199055-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bose was eager also to gain admission to a college at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199056&#95;116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199056-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was past the deadline for admission.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199056&#95;116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199056-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He sought help from some Indian students and from the Non-Collegiate Students Board. The Board offered the university's education at an economical cost without formal admission to a college. Bose <a href="/wiki/Matriculation#United_Kingdom" title="Matriculation">entered the register</a> of the university on 19 November 1919 and simultaneously set about preparing for the Civil Service exams.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199056&#95;116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199056-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He chose the Mental and Moral Sciences Tripos at Cambridge,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199056&#95;116-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199056-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> its completion requirement reduced to two years on account of his Indian B. A.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFay1995179&#95;117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFay1995179-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Subhas_C._Bose_003.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Subhas_C._Bose_003.jpg/250px-Subhas_C._Bose_003.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="358" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Subhas_C._Bose_003.jpg/500px-Subhas_C._Bose_003.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2200" data-file-height="3149" /></a><figcaption>Subhas Bose (standing, right) with friends in England, 1920</figcaption></figure><p>
There were six vacancies in the ICS.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199059&#95;118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199059-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Subhas Bose took the open competitive exam for them in August 1920 and was placed fourth.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199059&#95;118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199059-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This was a vital first step.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199059&#95;118-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199059-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Still remaining was a final examination in 1921 on more topics on India, including the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Penal_Code" title="Indian Penal Code">Indian Penal Code</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Evidence_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Evidence Act">Indian Evidence Act</a>, Indian history, and an Indian language.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199059&#95;118-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199059-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Successful candidates had also to clear a riding test. Having no fear of these subjects and being a rider, Subhas Bose felt the ICS was within easy reach.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199059&#95;118-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199059-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Yet between August 1920 and 1921 he began to have doubts about taking the final examination.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199059–60&#95;119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199059–60-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many letters were exchanged with his father and his brother <a href="/wiki/Sarat_Chandra_Bose" title="Sarat Chandra Bose">Sarat Chandra Bose</a> back in Calcutta.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199060&#95;120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199060-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In one letter to Sarat, Subhas wrote, </p><blockquote><p>"But for a man of my temperament who has been feeding on ideas that might be called eccentric—the line of least resistance is not the best line to follow ... The uncertainties of life are not appalling to one who has not, at heart, worldly ambitions. Moreover, it is not possible to serve one's country in the best and fullest manner if one is chained on to the civil service."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199060&#95;120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199060-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote><p> In April 1921, Subhas Bose made his decision firm not to take the final examination for the ICS and wrote to Sarat informing him of the same, apologising for the pain he would cause to his father, his mother, and other members of his family.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199061&#95;121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199061-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 22 April 1921, he wrote to the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_India" title="Secretary of State for India">Secretary of State for India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Montagu" title="Edwin Montagu">Edwin Montagu</a>, stating, "I wish to have my name removed from the list of probationers in the Indian Civil Service."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199062&#95;122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199062-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The following day he wrote again to Sarat:</p><blockquote><p>I received a letter from mother saying that in spite of what father and others think she prefers the ideals for which Mahatma Gandhi stands. I cannot tell you how happy I have been to receive such a letter. It will be worth a treasure for me as it has removed something like a burden from my mind."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199063&#95;123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199063-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>For some time before Subhas Bose had been in touch with <a href="/wiki/C._R._Das" class="mw-redirect" title="C. R. Das">C. R. Das</a>, a lawyer who had risen to the helm of politics in Bengal; Das encouraged Subhas to return to Calcutta.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199062–63&#95;124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199062–63-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> With the ICS decision now firmly behind him, Subhas Bose took his Cambridge B.A. Final examinations half-heartedly, passing, but being placed in the <a href="/wiki/British_undergraduate_degree_classification#Third-class_honours" title="British undergraduate degree classification">Third Class</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199063&#95;123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199063-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He prepared to sail for India in June 1921, electing for a fellow Indian student to pick up his diploma.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199062–63&#95;124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199062–63-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="1921–1932:_Indian_National_Congress"><span id="1921.E2.80.931932:_Indian_National_Congress"></span>1921–1932: Indian National Congress</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Subhas_Bose_at_inauguration_of_India_Society_Prague_1926.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Subhas_Bose_at_inauguration_of_India_Society_Prague_1926.jpg/250px-Subhas_Bose_at_inauguration_of_India_Society_Prague_1926.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="182" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Subhas_Bose_at_inauguration_of_India_Society_Prague_1926.jpg/500px-Subhas_Bose_at_inauguration_of_India_Society_Prague_1926.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="699" data-file-height="510" /></a><figcaption>Bose at the inauguration of the India Society in <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a> in 1926</figcaption></figure>
<p>Subhas Bose, aged 24, arrived ashore in India at Bombay on the morning of 16 July 1921 and immediately set about arranging an interview with Mahatma Gandhi. Gandhi, aged 51, was the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Non-cooperation_movement_(1909%E2%80%9322)" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-cooperation movement (1909–22)">non-cooperation movement</a> that had taken India by storm the previous year and in a quarter-century would evolve to secure its independence.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>al<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>am<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Gandhi happened to be in Bombay and agreed to see Bose that afternoon. In Bose's account of the meeting, written many years later, he pilloried Gandhi with question after question.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199069&#95;129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199069-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bose thought Gandhi's answers were vague, his goals unclear, his plan for achieving them not thought through.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199069&#95;129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199069-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Gandhi and Bose differed in this first meeting on the question of means—for Gandhi non-violent means to any end were non-negotiable; in Bose's thought, all means were acceptable in the service of anti-colonial ends.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199069&#95;129-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199069-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They differed on the question of ends—Bose was attracted to totalitarian models of governance, which were anathematised by Gandhi.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes20112&#95;130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes20112-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to historian Gordon, "Gandhi, however, set Bose on to the leader of the Congress and Indian nationalism in Bengal, C. R. Das, and in him Bose found the leader whom he sought."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199069&#95;129-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199069-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Das was more flexible than Gandhi, more sympathetic to the extremism that had attracted idealistic young men such as Bose in Bengal.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199069&#95;129-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199069-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Das launched Bose into nationalist politics.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199069&#95;129-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199069-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bose would work within the ambit of the Indian National Congress politics for nearly 20 years even as he tried to change its course.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199069&#95;129-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199069-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1922 Bose founded the newspaper <i>Swaraj</i> and assumed charge of the publicity for the Bengal Provincial Congress Committee.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEToye2007&#95;131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEToye2007-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His mentor was <a href="/wiki/Chittaranjan_Das" title="Chittaranjan Das">Chittaranjan Das</a>, a voice for aggressive nationalism in <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a>. In 1923, Bose was elected the President of <a href="/wiki/Indian_Youth_Congress" title="Indian Youth Congress">Indian Youth Congress</a> and also the Secretary of the Bengal State Congress. He became the editor of the newspaper "Forward", which had been founded by <a href="/wiki/Chittaranjan_Das" title="Chittaranjan Das">Chittaranjan Das</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEChakrabortyBhaṭṭācārya1989&#95;132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChakrabortyBhaṭṭācārya1989-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bose worked as the CEO of the <a href="/wiki/Calcutta_Municipal_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Calcutta Municipal Corporation">Calcutta Municipal Corporation</a> for Das when the latter was elected mayor of Calcutta in 1924.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEVas200832&#95;133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVas200832-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Das decided to choose Bose as the CEO over <a href="/wiki/Birendranath_Sasmal" title="Birendranath Sasmal">Birendranath Sasmal</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the same year, when Bose was leading a protest march in Calcutta, he, <a href="/wiki/Maghfoor_Ahmad_Ajazi" title="Maghfoor Ahmad Ajazi">Maghfoor Ahmad Ajazi</a> and other leaders were arrested and imprisoned.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Azadi&#95;ka&#95;Amrit&#95;Mahotsav&#95;135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Azadi_ka_Amrit_Mahotsav-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="the source only says that Ajazi was arrested (October 2023)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> After a roundup of nationalists in 1925, Bose was sent to prison in <a href="/wiki/Mandalay" title="Mandalay">Mandalay</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Burma" class="mw-redirect" title="British Burma">British Burma</a>, where he contracted <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEVipul2009116&#95;136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVipul2009116-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Subhas_C._Bose_001.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Subhas_C._Bose_001.jpg/250px-Subhas_C._Bose_001.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="175" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Subhas_C._Bose_001.jpg/500px-Subhas_C._Bose_001.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="3325" data-file-height="2331" /></a><figcaption>Subhas Bose (in military uniform) with Congress president, <a href="/wiki/Motilal_Nehru" title="Motilal Nehru">Motilal Nehru</a> taking the salute. Annual meeting, Indian National Congress, 29 December 1928</figcaption></figure><p>
In 1927, after being released from prison, Bose became general secretary of the Congress party and worked with Jawaharlal Nehru for independence. In late December 1928, Bose organised the Annual Meeting of the Indian National Congress in Calcutta.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990190&#95;137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990190-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His most memorable role was as <a href="/wiki/General_officer_commanding" title="General officer commanding">general officer commanding</a> (GOC) Congress Volunteer Corps.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990190&#95;137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990190-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Author <a href="/wiki/Nirad_Chaudhuri" class="mw-redirect" title="Nirad Chaudhuri">Nirad Chaudhuri</a> wrote about the meeting: </p><blockquote><p>Bose organized a volunteer corps in uniform, its officers were even provided with steel-cut epaulettes ... his uniform was made by a firm of British tailors in Calcutta, Harman's. A telegram addressed to him as GOC was delivered to the British General in <a href="/wiki/Fort_William,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort William, India">Fort William</a> and was the subject of a good deal of malicious gossip in the (British Indian) press. Mahatma Gandhi as a sincere pacifist vowed to non-violence, did not like the strutting, clicking of boots, and saluting, and he afterward described the Calcutta session of the Congress as a <a href="/wiki/Bertram_Mills" title="Bertram Mills">Bertram Mills circus</a>, which caused a great deal of indignation among the Bengalis.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990190&#95;137-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990190-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>A little later, Bose was again arrested and jailed for <a href="/wiki/Civil_disobedience" title="Civil disobedience">civil disobedience</a>; this time he emerged to become <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Kolkata" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayor of Kolkata">Mayor</a> of Calcutta in 1930.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEVipul2009116&#95;136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVipul2009116-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="1933–1937:_Illness,_Austria,_Emilie_Schenkl"><span id="1933.E2.80.931937:_Illness.2C_Austria.2C_Emilie_Schenkl"></span>1933–1937: Illness, Austria, Emilie Schenkl</h3></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1273380762/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti
