Bad Gastein, Austria, December 1937, with (left to right) <a href="/wiki/A._C._N._Nambiar" title="A. C. N. Nambiar">A. C. N. Nambiar</a> (Bose's second-in-command, Berlin, 1941–1945), Heidi Fulop-Miller, Schenkl, and Amiya Bose.</div></div></div></div>
<p>During the mid-1930s Bose travelled in Europe, visiting Indian students and European politicians, including <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>. He observed party organisation and saw communism and fascism in action.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In this period, he also researched and wrote the first part of his book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Indian_Struggle" title="The Indian Struggle">The Indian Struggle</a></i>, which covered the country's independence movement in the years 1920–1934. Although it was published in London in 1935, the British government banned the book in the colony out of fears that it would encourage unrest.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBoseBose1997&#95;139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoseBose1997-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bose was supported in Europe by the Indian Central European Society organised by <a href="/wiki/Otto_Faltis" title="Otto Faltis">Otto Faltis</a> from Vienna.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="1937–1940:_Indian_National_Congress"><span id="1937.E2.80.931940:_Indian_National_Congress"></span>1937–1940: Indian National Congress</h3></div>
<p>In 1938 Bose stated his opinion that the INC "should be organised on the broadest anti-imperialist front with the two-fold objective of winning political freedom and the establishment of a socialist regime."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBose2004&#95;141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBose2004-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By 1938 Bose had become a leader of national stature and agreed to accept nomination as Congress President. He stood for unqualified <a href="/wiki/Swaraj" title="Swaraj">Swaraj</a> (self-governance), including the use of force against the British. This meant a confrontation with Mohandas Gandhi, who in fact opposed Bose's presidency,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEJosh1992&#95;142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJosh1992-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> splitting the Indian National Congress party.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Subhas_Chandra_Bose_arrives_at_Dum_Dum_aerodrome.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_arrives_at_Dum_Dum_aerodrome.jpg/250px-Subhas_Chandra_Bose_arrives_at_Dum_Dum_aerodrome.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="321" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_arrives_at_Dum_Dum_aerodrome.jpg/400px-Subhas_Chandra_Bose_arrives_at_Dum_Dum_aerodrome.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/54/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_arrives_at_Dum_Dum_aerodrome.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="514" /></a><figcaption>Bose, president-elect, INC, arrives in Calcutta, 24 January 1938, after two-month vacation in Austria.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>an<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>ao<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>Bose attempted to maintain unity, but Gandhi advised Bose to form his own cabinet. The rift also divided Bose and Nehru; he appeared at the 1939 Congress meeting on a stretcher. He was elected president again over Gandhi's preferred candidate <a href="/wiki/Pattabhi_Sitaramayya" class="mw-redirect" title="Pattabhi Sitaramayya">Pattabhi Sitaramayya</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEChattopadhyay1989&#95;147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChattopadhyay1989-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/U._Muthuramalingam_Thevar" class="mw-redirect" title="U. Muthuramalingam Thevar">U. Muthuramalingam Thevar</a> strongly supported Bose in the intra-Congress dispute. Thevar mobilised all south India votes for Bose.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEPhadnis2009185&#95;148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhadnis2009185-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, due to the manoeuvrings of the Gandhi-led clique in the Congress Working Committee, Bose found himself forced to resign from the Congress presidency.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>On 22 June 1939 Bose organised the <a href="/wiki/All_India_Forward_Bloc" title="All India Forward Bloc">All India Forward Bloc</a> a faction within the Indian National Congress,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEPadhy2011234&#95;149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPadhy2011234-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> aimed at consolidating the political left, but its main strength was in his home state, Bengal. U Muthuramalingam Thevar, who was a staunch supporter of Bose from the beginning, joined the Forward Bloc. When Bose visited Madurai on 6 September, Thevar organised a massive rally as his reception.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>When Subhas Chandra Bose was heading to Madurai, on an invitation of <a href="/wiki/Muthuramalinga_Thevar" class="mw-redirect" title="Muthuramalinga Thevar">Muthuramalinga Thevar</a> to amass support for the Forward Bloc, he passed through Madras and spent three days at Gandhi Peak.
His correspondence reveals that despite his clear dislike for British subjugation, he was deeply impressed by their methodical and systematic approach and their steadfastly disciplinarian outlook towards life. In England, he exchanged ideas on the future of India with British <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a> leaders and political thinkers like <a href="/wiki/Edward_Wood,_1st_Earl_of_Halifax" title="Edward Wood, 1st Earl of Halifax">Lord Halifax</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Lansbury" title="George Lansbury">George Lansbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clement_Attlee" title="Clement Attlee">Clement Attlee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Greenwood" title="Arthur Greenwood">Arthur Greenwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Laski" title="Harold Laski">Harold Laski</a>, <a href="/wiki/J.B.S._Haldane" class="mw-redirect" title="J.B.S. Haldane">J.B.S. Haldane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Jennings" title="Ivor Jennings">Ivor Jennings</a>, <a href="/wiki/G.D.H._Cole" class="mw-redirect" title="G.D.H. Cole">G.D.H. Cole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Murray" title="Gilbert Murray">Gilbert Murray</a> and Sir <a href="/wiki/Stafford_Cripps" title="Stafford Cripps">Stafford Cripps</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Bose_AICC_meeting_1939.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Bose_AICC_meeting_1939.jpg/250px-Bose_AICC_meeting_1939.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="168" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Bose_AICC_meeting_1939.jpg/500px-Bose_AICC_meeting_1939.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="673" /></a><figcaption>Bose arriving at the 1939 annual session of the Congress, where he was re-elected, but later had to resign after disagreements with Gandhi and the Congress High Command</figcaption></figure>
<p>He came to believe that an independent India needed socialist authoritarianism, on the lines of Turkey's <a href="/wiki/Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" class="mw-redirect" title="Kemal Atatürk">Kemal Atatürk</a>, for at least two decades. For political reasons Bose was refused permission by the British authorities to meet Atatürk at <a href="/wiki/Ankara" title="Ankara">Ankara</a>. During his sojourn in England Bose tried to schedule appointments with several politicians, but only the Labour Party and <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(UK)" title="Liberal Party (UK)">Liberal</a> politicians agreed to meet with him. <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a> officials refused to meet him or show him courtesy because he was a politician coming from a colony. In the 1930s leading figures in the Conservative Party had opposed even <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominion</a> status for India. It was during the Labour Party government of 1945–1951, with Attlee as the Prime Minister, that India gained independence.
</p><p>On the outbreak of war, Bose advocated a campaign of mass civil disobedience to protest against Viceroy <a href="/wiki/Lord_Linlithgow" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Linlithgow">Lord Linlithgow</a>'s decision to declare war on India's behalf without consulting the Congress leadership. Having failed to persuade Gandhi of the necessity of this, Bose organised mass protests in Calcutta calling for the removal of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Hole_of_Calcutta#Monument_to_the_victims" title="Black Hole of Calcutta">"Holwell Monument"</a>, which then stood at the corner of <a href="/wiki/Dalhousie_Square" class="mw-redirect" title="Dalhousie Square">Dalhousie Square</a> in memoriam of those who died in the <a href="/wiki/Black_Hole_of_Calcutta" title="Black Hole of Calcutta">Black Hole of Calcutta</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTESen1999&#95;150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESen1999-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He was thrown in jail by the British, but was released following a seven-day hunger strike. Bose's house in Calcutta was kept under surveillance by the <a href="/wiki/Criminal_Investigation_Department" title="Criminal Investigation Department">CID</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEDurga&#95;Das&#95;Pvt.&#95;Ltd1985&#95;151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDurga_Das_Pvt._Ltd1985-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="1941:_Escape_to_Nazi_Germany">1941: Escape to Nazi Germany</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Wanderer_BLA.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Wanderer_BLA.jpg/250px-Wanderer_BLA.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Wanderer_BLA.jpg/500px-Wanderer_BLA.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="4160" data-file-height="3120" /></a><figcaption>The Wanderer car Bose used to escape from his Calcutta home in 1941</figcaption></figure>
<p>Bose's arrest and subsequent release set the scene for his escape to Nazi Germany, via <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> and the Soviet Union. A few days before his escape, he sought solitude and, on this pretext, avoided meeting British guards and grew a beard. Late night 16 January 1941, the night of his escape, he dressed as a <a href="/wiki/Pathan" class="mw-redirect" title="Pathan">Pathan</a> (brown long coat, a black fez-type coat and broad pyjamas) to avoid being identified. Bose escaped from under British surveillance from his Elgin Road house in Calcutta on the night of 17 January 1941, accompanied by his nephew <a href="/wiki/Sisir_Kumar_Bose" title="Sisir Kumar Bose">Sisir Kumar Bose</a>, later reaching Gomoh Railway Station (now <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Subhas_Chandra_Bose_Gomoh_railway_station" title="Netaji Subhas Chandra Bose Gomoh railway station">Netaji Subhas Chandra Bose Gomoh Station</a>) in the then state of Bihar (now <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a>), India.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELoiwal2017a&#95;152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELoiwal2017a-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELoiwal2017b&#95;153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELoiwal2017b-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTETalwar1976&#95;154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETalwar1976-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMarkandeya1990&#95;155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarkandeya1990-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Bose journeyed to <a href="/wiki/Peshawar" title="Peshawar">Peshawar</a> with the help of the <a href="/wiki/Abwehr" title="Abwehr">Abwehr</a>, where he was met by Akbar Shah, Mohammed Shah and <a href="/wiki/Bhagat_Ram_Talwar" title="Bhagat Ram Talwar">Bhagat Ram Talwar</a>. Bose was taken to the home of Abad Khan, a trusted friend of Akbar Shah's. On 26 January 1941, Bose began his journey to reach Russia through <a href="/wiki/British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="British India">British India</a>'s <a href="/wiki/North-West_Frontier_Province_(1901%E2%80%931955)" class="mw-redirect" title="North-West Frontier Province (1901–1955)">North West frontier</a> with Afghanistan. For this reason, he enlisted the help of Mian Akbar Shah, then a Forward Bloc leader in the North-West Frontier Province. Shah had been out of India en route to the Soviet Union and suggested a novel disguise for Bose to assume. Since Bose could not speak <a href="/wiki/Pashto_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Pashto language">Pashto</a>, it would have made him an easy target of Pashto speakers working for the British. For this reason, Shah suggested that Bose act deaf and dumb, and let his beard grow to mimic those of the tribesmen. Bose's guide <a href="/wiki/Bhagat_Ram_Talwar" title="Bhagat Ram Talwar">Bhagat Ram Talwar</a>, unknown to him, was a Soviet agent.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTETalwar1976&#95;154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETalwar1976-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMarkandeya1990&#95;155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarkandeya1990-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEJames1997554&#95;156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJames1997554-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Supporters of the <a href="/wiki/Aga_Khan_III" title="Aga Khan III">Aga Khan III</a> helped him across the border into <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> where he was met by an Abwehr unit posing as a party of road construction engineers from the <a href="/wiki/Organization_Todt" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization Todt">Organization Todt</a> who then aided his passage across Afghanistan via <a href="/wiki/Kabul" title="Kabul">Kabul</a> to the border with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. After assuming the guise of a <a href="/wiki/Pashtun_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Pashtun people">Pashtun</a> insurance agent ("Ziaudddin") to reach Afghanistan, Bose changed his guise and travelled to Moscow on the Italian passport of an Italian nobleman "Count Orlando Mazzotta". From Moscow, he reached <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, and from there he travelled to <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTETalwar1976&#95;154-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETalwar1976-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMarkandeya1990&#95;155-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarkandeya1990-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEThomson2004&#95;157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomson2004-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Once in Russia the <a href="/wiki/NKVD" title="NKVD">NKVD</a> transported Bose to <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> where he hoped that Russia's historical enmity to British rule in India would result in support for his plans for a popular rising in India. However, Bose found the Soviets' response disappointing and was rapidly passed over to the German Ambassador in Moscow, <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Werner_von_der_Schulenburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Friedrich Werner von der Schulenburg">Count von der Schulenburg</a>. He had Bose flown on to <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> in a special courier aircraft at the beginning of April where he was to receive a more favourable hearing from <a href="/wiki/Joachim_von_Ribbentrop" title="Joachim von Ribbentrop">Joachim von Ribbentrop</a> and the Foreign Ministry officials at the <a href="/wiki/Wilhelmstrasse" title="Wilhelmstrasse">Wilhelmstrasse</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTETalwar1976&#95;154-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETalwar1976-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMarkandeya1990&#95;155-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarkandeya1990-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMajumdar199710–14&#95;158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMajumdar199710–14-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="1941–1943:_Collaboration_with_Nazi_Germany"><span id="1941.E2.80.931943:_Collaboration_with_Nazi_Germany"></span>1941–1943: Collaboration with Nazi Germany</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1273380762/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" /><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:432px;max-width:432px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:213px;max-width:213px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:143px;overflow:hidden"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Alber-064-03A,_Subhas_Chandra_Bose_bei_Heinrich_Himmler.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Alber-064-03A%2C_Subhas_Chandra_Bose_bei_Heinrich_Himmler.jpg/250px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Alber-064-03A%2C_Subhas_Chandra_Bose_bei_Heinrich_Himmler.jpg" decoding="async" width="211" height="144" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Alber-064-03A%2C_Subhas_Chandra_Bose_bei_Heinrich_Himmler.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Alber-064-03A%2C_Subhas_Chandra_Bose_bei_Heinrich_Himmler.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Alber-064-03A%2C_Subhas_Chandra_Bose_bei_Heinrich_Himmler.jpg/500px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Alber-064-03A%2C_Subhas_Chandra_Bose_bei_Heinrich_Himmler.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4015" data-file-height="2742" /></a></span></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:215px;max-width:215px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:143px;overflow:hidden"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Subhas_Chandra_Bose_meeting_Adolf_Hitler.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_meeting_Adolf_Hitler.jpg/250px-Subhas_Chandra_Bose_meeting_Adolf_Hitler.jpg" decoding="async" width="213" height="144" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_meeting_Adolf_Hitler.jpg/330px-Subhas_Chandra_Bose_meeting_Adolf_Hitler.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_meeting_Adolf_Hitler.jpg/500px-Subhas_Chandra_Bose_meeting_Adolf_Hitler.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="539" /></a></span></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">(left) Bose with <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler" title="Heinrich Himmler">Heinrich Himmler</a>, head of the <a href="/wiki/SS" class="mw-redirect" title="SS">SS</a>; (right) Bose meeting <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>In Germany, Bose was attached to the <a href="/wiki/Special_Bureau_for_India" title="Special Bureau for India">Special Bureau for India</a> under <a href="/wiki/Adam_von_Trott_zu_Solz" title="Adam von Trott zu Solz">Adam von Trott zu Solz</a> which was responsible for broadcasting on the German-sponsored <a href="/wiki/Azad_Hind_Radio" title="Azad Hind Radio">Azad Hind Radio</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEEncyclopædia&#95;Britannica2016&#95;159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEncyclopædia_Britannica2016-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He founded the Free India Centre in Berlin and created the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Legion" title="Indian Legion">Indian Legion</a> (consisting of some 4500 soldiers) out of Indian prisoners of war who had previously fought for the British in <a href="/wiki/North_African_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="North African Campaign">North Africa</a> prior to their capture by Axis forces. The Indian Legion was attached to the Wehrmacht, and later transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Waffen_SS" class="mw-redirect" title="Waffen SS">Waffen SS</a>. Its members swore the following allegiance to Hitler and Bose: "I swear by God this holy oath that I will obey the leader of the German race and state, <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>, as the commander of the German armed forces in the fight for India, whose leader is Subhas Chandra Bose". This oath clearly abrogated control of the Indian legion to the German armed forces whilst stating Bose's overall leadership of India. He was also, however, prepared to envisage an invasion of India via the USSR by Nazi troops, spearheaded by the <a href="/wiki/Indische_Legion" class="mw-redirect" title="Indische Legion">Azad Hind Legion</a>; many have questioned his judgment here, as it seems unlikely that the Germans could have been easily persuaded to leave after such an invasion, which might also have resulted in an Axis victory in the War.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEThomson2004&#95;157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomson2004-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Soon, according to historian Romain Hayes, "the (German) Foreign Office procured a luxurious residence for (Bose) along with a butler, cook, gardener, and an SS-chauffeured car. Emilie Schenkl moved in openly with him. The Germans, aware of the nature of the relationship, refrained from any involvement."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes201167&#95;160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes201167-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, most of the staff in the <a href="/wiki/Special_Bureau_for_India" title="Special Bureau for India">Special Bureau for India</a>, which had been set up to aid Bose, did not get along with Emilie.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990446&#95;161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990446-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In particular <a href="/wiki/Adam_von_Trott_zu_Solz" title="Adam von Trott zu Solz">Adam von Trott</a>, Alexander Werth and Freda Kretschemer, according to historian <a href="/wiki/Leonard_A._Gordon" title="Leonard A. Gordon">Leonard A. Gordon</a>, "appear to have disliked her intensely. They believed that she and Bose were not married and that she was using her liaison with Bose to live an especially comfortable life during the hard times of war" and that differences were compounded by issues of class.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990446&#95;161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990446-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In November 1942, Schenkl gave birth to their daughter.
</p><p>The Germans were unwilling to form an alliance with Bose because they considered him unpopular in comparison with Mahatma Gandhi and Jawaharlal Nehru.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-visionideas&#95;162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visionideas-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes2011111&#95;163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes2011111-163"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By the spring of 1942, the German army was <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)#Don,_Volga,_and_Caucasus:_Summer_1942" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">mired in the USSR</a>. Bose, due to disappointment over the lack of response from Nazi Germany, was now keen to move to Southeast Asia, where Japan had just won quick victories. However, he still expected official recognition from Nazi Germany. <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> during his only meeting with Bose in late May 1942 refused to entertain Bose's requests and facilitated him with a submarine voyage to East Asia.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes2011114–116&#95;65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes2011114–116-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Ashis&#95;164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ashis-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Dunphy&#95;165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dunphy-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In February 1943, Bose left Schenkl and their baby daughter and boarded a German submarine to travel, via transfer to a Japanese submarine, to Japanese-occupied southeast Asia. In all, 3,000 Indian prisoners of war signed up for the Free India Legion. But instead of being delighted, Bose was worried. A left-wing admirer of Russia, he was devastated when Hitler's tanks rolled across the Soviet border. Matters were worsened by the fact that the now-retreating German army would be in no position to offer him help in driving the British from India. When he met Hitler in May 1942, his suspicions were confirmed, and he came to believe that the Nazi leader was more interested in using his men to win propaganda victories than military ones. So, in February 1943, Bose boarded a German <a href="/wiki/U-boat" title="U-boat">U-boat</a> and left for Japan. This left the men he had recruited leaderless and demoralised in Germany.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEThomson2004&#95;157-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomson2004-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHauner198128–29&#95;166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHauner198128–29-166"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="1943–1945:_Japanese-occupied_Asia"><span id="1943.E2.80.931945:_Japanese-occupied_Asia"></span>1943–1945: Japanese-occupied Asia</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Army" title="Indian National Army">Indian National Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azad_Hind" title="Azad Hind">Azad Hind</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:19430428_japanese_submarine_crew_i-29.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/19430428_japanese_submarine_crew_i-29.png/250px-19430428_japanese_submarine_crew_i-29.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="292" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/19430428_japanese_submarine_crew_i-29.png/500px-19430428_japanese_submarine_crew_i-29.png 1.5x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="760" /></a><figcaption>The crew of Japanese submarine I-29 after the rendezvous with German submarine U-180 300 sm southeast of <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>; Bose is sitting in the front row (28 April 1943)</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1943, after being disillusioned that Germany could be of any help in gaining India's independence, Bose left for Japan. He travelled with the German submarine <a href="/wiki/U-180" class="mw-redirect" title="U-180">U-180</a> around the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a> to the southeast of Madagascar, where he was transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_submarine_I-29" title="Japanese submarine I-29"><i>I-29</i></a> for the rest of the journey to <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Japan">Imperial Japan</a>. This was the only civilian transfer between two submarines of two different navies in World War II.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTETalwar1976&#95;154-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETalwar1976-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMarkandeya1990&#95;155-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarkandeya1990-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Army" title="Indian National Army">Indian National Army</a> (INA) was the brainchild of Japanese Major (and post-war Lieutenant-General) <a href="/wiki/Iwaichi_Fujiwara" title="Iwaichi Fujiwara">Iwaichi Fujiwara</a>, head of the Japanese intelligence unit <a href="/wiki/Fujiwara_Kikan" class="mw-redirect" title="Fujiwara Kikan">Fujiwara Kikan</a>. Fujiwara's mission was "to raise an army which would fight alongside the Japanese army."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFay199574–75&#95;167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFay199574–75-167"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a21–23&#95;168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a21–23-168"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He first met <a href="/wiki/Giani_Pritam_Singh_Dhillon" title="Giani Pritam Singh Dhillon">Pritam Singh Dhillon</a>, the president of the <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a> chapter of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Independence_League" title="Indian Independence League">Indian Independence League</a>, and through Pritam Singh's network recruited a captured British Indian army captain, <a href="/wiki/General_Mohan_Singh" class="mw-redirect" title="General Mohan Singh">Mohan Singh</a>, on the western <a href="/wiki/Malayan_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Malayan peninsula">Malayan peninsula</a> in December 1941. The <a href="/wiki/First_Indian_National_Army" title="First Indian National Army">First Indian National Army</a> was formed as a result of discussion between Fujiwara and Mohan Singh in the second half of December 1941, and the name chosen jointly by them in the first week of January 1942.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a24–25&#95;169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a24–25-169"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>This was along the concept of, and with support of, what was then known as the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Independence_League" title="Indian Independence League">Indian Independence League</a> headed from Tokyo by expatriate nationalist leader <a href="/wiki/Rash_Behari_Bose" title="Rash Behari Bose">Rash Behari Bose</a>. The first INA was however disbanded in December 1942 after disagreements between the <a href="/wiki/Hikari_Kikan" title="Hikari Kikan">Hikari Kikan</a> and Mohan Singh, who came to believe that the Japanese High Command was using the INA as a mere pawn and propaganda tool. Singh was taken into custody and the troops returned to the prisoner-of-war camp. However, the idea of an independence army was revived with the arrival of Subhas Chandra Bose in the Far East in 1943. In July, at a meeting in Singapore, Rash Behari Bose handed over control of the organisation to Subhas Chandra Bose. Bose was able to reorganise the fledgling army and organise massive support among the expatriate Indian population in south-east Asia, who lent their support by both enlisting in the Indian National Army, as well as financially in response to Bose's calls for sacrifice for the independence cause. INA had a separate women's unit, the <a href="/wiki/Rani_of_Jhansi_Regiment" title="Rani of Jhansi Regiment">Rani of Jhansi Regiment</a> (named after Rani <a href="/wiki/Lakshmi_Bai" class="mw-redirect" title="Lakshmi Bai">Lakshmi Bai</a>) headed by Capt. <a href="/wiki/Lakshmi_Sahgal" title="Lakshmi Sahgal">Lakshmi Swaminathan</a>, which is seen as a first of its kind in Asia.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBose2002&#95;170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBose2002-170"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTETarique&#95;171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETarique-171"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Azad_Hind_Currency.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Azad_Hind_Currency.jpg/250px-Azad_Hind_Currency.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="161" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Azad_Hind_Currency.jpg/500px-Azad_Hind_Currency.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2526" data-file-height="1622" /></a><figcaption>Currency issued by the <a href="/wiki/Azad_Hind_Bank" title="Azad Hind Bank">Azad Hind Bank</a> with Bose's portrait</figcaption></figure>
<p>Even when faced with military reverses, Bose was able to maintain support for the <a href="/wiki/Azad_Hind" title="Azad Hind">Azad Hind</a> movement. Spoken as a part of a motivational speech for the Indian National Army at a rally of Indians in <a href="/wiki/Burma" class="mw-redirect" title="Burma">Burma</a> on 4 July 1944, Bose's most famous quote was "Give me blood, and I shall give you freedom!" In this, he urged the people of India to join him in his fight against the British Raj.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Spoken in Hindi, Bose's words are highly evocative. The troops of the INA were under the aegis of a provisional government, the Azad Hind Government, which came to produce its own currency, postage stamps, court and civil code, and was recognised by nine Axis states—Germany, Japan, <a href="/wiki/Italian_Social_Republic" title="Italian Social Republic">Italian Social Republic</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Independent State of Croatia">Independent State of Croatia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wang_Jingwei_regime" title="Wang Jingwei regime">Wang Jingwei regime</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a>, China, a provisional government of Burma, <a href="/wiki/Manchukuo" title="Manchukuo">Manchukuo</a> and Japanese-controlled <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. Of those countries, five were authorities established under Axis occupation. This government participated in the so-called <a href="/wiki/Greater_East_Asia_Conference" title="Greater East Asia Conference">Greater East Asia Conference</a> as an observer in November 1943.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGotoKratoska200357–58&#95;172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGotoKratoska200357–58-172"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The INA's first commitment was in the Japanese thrust towards Eastern Indian frontiers of <a href="/wiki/Manipur" title="Manipur">Manipur</a>. INA's special forces, the <a href="/wiki/Bahadur_Group" title="Bahadur Group">Bahadur Group</a>, were involved in operations behind enemy lines both during the diversionary attacks in Arakan, as well as the Japanese thrust towards <a href="/wiki/Imphal" title="Imphal">Imphal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kohima" title="Kohima">Kohima</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Subhas_Chandra_1943_Tokyo.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Subhas_Chandra_1943_Tokyo.jpg/250px-Subhas_Chandra_1943_Tokyo.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="176" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Subhas_Chandra_1943_Tokyo.jpg/500px-Subhas_Chandra_1943_Tokyo.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="528" /></a><figcaption>Bose speaking in Tokyo in 1943</figcaption></figure>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_the_Andaman_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese occupation of the Andaman Islands">Japanese also took possession of Andaman and Nicobar Islands</a> in 1942 and a year later, the Provisional Government and the INA were established in the <a href="/wiki/Andaman_and_Nicobar_Islands" title="Andaman and Nicobar Islands">Andaman and Nicobar Islands</a> with Lt Col. <a href="/wiki/Arcot_Doraiswamy_Loganadan" class="mw-redirect" title="Arcot Doraiswamy Loganadan">Arcot Doraiswamy Loganadan</a> appointed its Governor General. The islands were renamed <i>Shaheed</i> (Martyr) and <i>Swaraj</i> (Independence). However, the Japanese Navy remained in essential control of the island's administration. During Bose's only visit to the islands in early 1944, apparently in the interest of shielding Bose from attaining a full knowledge of ultimate Japanese intentions, his Japanese hosts carefully isolated him from the local population. At that time the island's Japanese administration had been torturing the leader of the island's Indian Independence League, <a href="/wiki/Diwan_Singh" title="Diwan Singh">Diwan Singh</a>, who later died of his injuries in the <a href="/wiki/Cellular_Jail" title="Cellular Jail">Cellular Jail</a>. During Bose's visit to the islands several locals attempted to alert Bose to Singh's plight, but apparently without success. During this time Loganathan became aware of his lack of any genuine administrative control and resigned in protest as Governor General, later returning to the Government's headquarters in Rangoon.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTESingh249&#95;174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESingh249-174"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper2007325&#95;175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper2007325-175"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On the Indian mainland, an Indian Tricolour flag, modelled after that of the Indian National Congress, was raised for the first time in the town of <a href="/wiki/Moirang" title="Moirang">Moirang</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Manipur" title="Manipur">Manipur</a>, in north-eastern India. The adjacent towns of Kohima and Imphal were then encircled and placed under siege by divisions of the Japanese Army, working in conjunction with the Burmese National Army, and with Brigades of the INA, known as the Gandhi and Nehru Brigades. This attempt at conquering the Indian mainland had the Axis codename of <a href="/wiki/Operation_U-Go" title="Operation U-Go">Operation U-Go</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>During this operation, on 6 July 1944, in a speech broadcast by the <a href="/wiki/Azad_Hind_Radio" title="Azad Hind Radio">Azad Hind Radio</a> from Singapore, Bose addressed Mahatma Gandhi as the "Father of the Nation" and asked for his blessings and good wishes for the war he was fighting. This was the first time that Gandhi was referred to by this appellation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The protracted Japanese attempts to take these two towns depleted Japanese resources, with Operation U-Go ultimately proving unsuccessful. Through several months of Japanese onslaught on these two towns, Commonwealth forces remained entrenched in the towns. Commonwealth forces then counter-attacked, inflicting serious losses on the Axis led forces, who were then forced into a retreat back into Burmese territory. After the Japanese defeat at the battles of Kohima and Imphal, Bose's Provisional Government's aim of establishing a base in mainland India was lost forever.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Still the INA fought in key battles against the British Indian Army in Burmese territory, notable in Meiktilla, <a href="/wiki/Mandalay" title="Mandalay">Mandalay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pegu" class="mw-redirect" title="Pegu">Pegu</a>, Nyangyu and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Popa" title="Mount Popa">Mount Popa</a>. However, with the fall of <a href="/wiki/Rangoon" class="mw-redirect" title="Rangoon">Rangoon</a>, Bose's government ceased to be an effective political entity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> A large proportion of the INA troops surrendered under Lt Col Loganathan. The remaining troops retreated with Bose towards <a href="/wiki/British_Malaya" title="British Malaya">Malaya</a> or made for <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>. Japan's surrender at the end of the war also led to the surrender of the remaining elements of the Indian National Army. The INA prisoners were then repatriated to India and some <a href="/wiki/INA_trials" class="mw-redirect" title="INA trials">tried for treason</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-White-Spunner&#95;2017&#95;p.&#95;13&#95;177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-White-Spunner_2017_p._13-177"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="18_August_1945:_Death">18 August 1945: Death</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Subhas_Chandra_Bose" title="Death of Subhas Chandra Bose">Death of Subhas Chandra Bose</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1273380762/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" /><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" decoding="async" width="213" height="281" class="mw-file-element"
