2x" data-file-width="1102" data-file-height="1452" /></a></span></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:213px;max-width:213px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:280px;overflow:hidden"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Subhas_Chandra_Bose_(tokyo).JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_%28tokyo%29.JPG/250px-Subhas_Chandra_Bose_%28tokyo%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="211" height="281" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_%28tokyo%29.JPG/330px-Subhas_Chandra_Bose_%28tokyo%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_%28tokyo%29.JPG/500px-Subhas_Chandra_Bose_%28tokyo%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a></span></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">(left) The last aeroplane journeys of Subhas Chandra Bose; flight paths: blue (completed), red (not completed); (right) A memorial to Subhas Chandra Bose in the <a href="/wiki/Renk%C5%8Dji_Temple" class="mw-redirect" title="Renkōji Temple">Renkōji Temple</a>, Tokyo. Bose's ashes are stored in the temple in a golden pagoda</div></div></div></div>
<p>Subhas Chandra Bose died on 18 August 1945 from third-degree burns after his airplane crashed in <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_under_Japanese_rule" title="Taiwan under Japanese rule">Japanese-ruled Formosa</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper20072&#95;178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper20072-178"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBandyopadhyay2004427&#95;24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBandyopadhyay2004427-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-dod-combined&#95;6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dod-combined-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-gordon-bose-death&#95;7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gordon-bose-death-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, many among his supporters, especially in Bengal, refused at the time, and have refused since, to believe either the fact or the circumstances of his death.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper20072&#95;178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper20072-178"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200722&#95;81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200722-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEWolpert2000339–340&#95;83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolpert2000339–340-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Conspiracy theories appeared within hours of his death and have persisted thereafter,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper20072&#95;178-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper20072-178"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>ap<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> keeping alive various martial myths about Bose.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMetcalfMetcalf2012210&#95;20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMetcalfMetcalf2012210-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Taipei" title="Taipei">Taihoku</a>, at around 2:30<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>pm as the bomber with Bose on board was leaving the standard path taken by aircraft during take-off, the passengers inside heard a loud sound, similar to an engine backfiring.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990540&#95;180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990540-180"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFay1995384&#95;181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFay1995384-181"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The mechanics on the tarmac saw something fall out of the plane.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197&#95;182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was the portside engine, or a part of it, and the propeller.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197&#95;182-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990540&#95;180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990540-180"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The plane swung wildly to the right and plummeted, crashing, breaking into two, and exploding into flames.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197&#95;182-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990540&#95;180-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990540-180"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Inside, the chief pilot, copilot and Lieutenant-General <a href="/wiki/Tsunamasa_Shidei" title="Tsunamasa Shidei">Tsunamasa Shidei</a>, the Vice Chief of Staff of the Japanese Kwantung Army, who was to have made the negotiations for Bose with the Soviet army in Manchuria,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a195–196&#95;183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a195–196-183"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> were instantly killed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197&#95;182-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541&#95;184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541-184"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bose's assistant <a href="/wiki/Raja_Habib_ur_Rahman_Khan" class="mw-redirect" title="Raja Habib ur Rahman Khan">Habibur Rahman</a> was stunned, passing out briefly, and Bose, although conscious and not fatally hurt, was soaked in gasoline.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197&#95;182-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> When Rahman came to, he and Bose attempted to leave by the rear door, but found it blocked by the luggage.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541&#95;184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541-184"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They then decided to run through the flames and exit from the front.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541&#95;184-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541-184"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The ground staff, now approaching the plane, saw two people staggering towards them, one of whom had become a human torch.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197&#95;182-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The human torch turned out to be Bose, whose gasoline-soaked clothes had instantly ignited.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541&#95;184-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541-184"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Rahman and a few others managed to smother the flames, but also noticed that Bose's face and head appeared badly burned.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541&#95;184-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541-184"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to Joyce Chapman Lebra, "A truck which served as ambulance rushed Bose and the other passengers to the Nanmon Military Hospital south of Taihoku."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197&#95;182-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The airport personnel called Dr. Taneyoshi Yoshimi, the surgeon-in-charge at the hospital at around 3<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>pm.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541&#95;184-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541-184"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bose was conscious and mostly coherent when they reached the hospital, and for some time thereafter.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541–542&#95;185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541–542-185"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bose was naked, except for a blanket wrapped around him, and Dr. Yoshimi immediately saw evidence of third-degree burns on many parts of the body, especially on his chest, doubting very much that he would live.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541–542&#95;185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541–542-185"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Dr. Yoshimi promptly began to treat Bose and was assisted by Dr. Tsuruta.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541–542&#95;185-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990541–542-185"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to historian <a href="/wiki/Leonard_A._Gordon" title="Leonard A. Gordon">Leonard A. Gordon</a>, who interviewed all the hospital personnel later,
</p>
<blockquote><p>A disinfectant, <a href="/wiki/Ethacridine_lactate" title="Ethacridine lactate">Rivamol</a> &#32;&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>&#93;, was put over most of his body and then a white ointment was applied and he was bandaged over most of his body. Dr. Yoshimi gave Bose four injections of <a href="/wiki/Camphor#Medicinal_uses" title="Camphor">Vita Camphor</a> and two of <a href="/wiki/Digitalis#Cardiac" title="Digitalis">Digitamine</a> for his weakened heart. These were given about every 30 minutes. Since his body had lost fluids quickly upon being burnt, he was also given <a href="/wiki/Ringer%27s_solution" title="Ringer&#39;s solution">Ringer solution</a> intravenously. A third doctor, Dr. Ishii gave him a blood transfusion. An orderly, Kazuo Mitsui, an army private, was in the room and several nurses were also assisting. Bose still had a clear head which Dr. Yoshimi found remarkable for someone with such severe injuries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990542&#95;186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990542-186"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Soon, in spite of the treatment, Bose went into a coma.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990542&#95;186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990542-186"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197&#95;182-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A few hours later, between 9 and 10&#160;pm (local time) on Saturday, 18 August 1945, Bose died aged 48.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990542&#95;186-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990542-186"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197&#95;182-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Bose's body was cremated in the main Taihoku crematorium two days later, 20 August 1945.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990543&#95;187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990543-187"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 23 August 1945, the Japanese news agency Do Trzei announced the death of Bose and Shidea.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197&#95;182-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a196–197-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 7 September a Japanese officer, Lieutenant Tatsuo Hayashida, carried Bose's ashes to Tokyo, and the following morning they were handed to the president of the Tokyo Indian Independence League, Rama Murti.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990544–545&#95;188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990544–545-188"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 14 September a memorial service was held for Bose in Tokyo and a few days later the ashes were turned over to the priest of the <a href="/wiki/Renk%C5%8Dji_Temple" class="mw-redirect" title="Renkōji Temple">Renkōji Temple</a> of <a href="/wiki/Nichiren_Buddhism" title="Nichiren Buddhism">Nichiren Buddhism</a> in Tokyo.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTELebra2008a197–198&#95;189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebra2008a197–198-189"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990545&#95;190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990545-190"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There they have remained ever since.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990545&#95;190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990545-190"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Among the INA personnel, there was widespread disbelief, shock, and trauma. Most affected were the young Tamil Indians from Malaya and Singapore, both men and women, who comprised the bulk of the civilians who had enlisted in the INA.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200721&#95;87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200721-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The professional soldiers in the INA, most of whom were Punjabis, faced an uncertain future, with many fatalistically expecting reprisals from the British.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200721&#95;87-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200721-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In India the Indian National Congress's official line was succinctly expressed in a letter Mohandas Karamchand (Mahatma) Gandhi wrote to <a href="/wiki/Rajkumari_Amrit_Kaur" class="mw-redirect" title="Rajkumari Amrit Kaur">Rajkumari Amrit Kaur</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200721&#95;87-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200721-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Said Gandhi, "Subhas Bose has died well. He was undoubtedly a patriot, though misguided."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200721&#95;87-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200721-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many congressmen had not forgiven Bose for quarrelling with Gandhi and for collaborating with what they considered was <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japanese</a> fascism. The Indian soldiers in the British Indian army, some two and a half million of whom had fought during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, were conflicted about the INA. Some saw the INA as traitors and wanted them punished; others felt more sympathetic. The British Raj, though never seriously threatened by the INA, tried 300 INA officers for treason in the <a href="/wiki/INA_trials" class="mw-redirect" title="INA trials">INA trials</a>, but eventually backtracked.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200721&#95;87-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylyHarper200721-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Ideology">Ideology</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Political_views_of_Subhas_Chandra_Bose" title="Political views of Subhas Chandra Bose">Political views of Subhas Chandra Bose</a></div>
<p>Subhas Chandra Bose believed that the <a href="/wiki/Bhagavad_Gita" title="Bhagavad Gita">Bhagavad Gita</a> was a great source of inspiration for the struggle against the British.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTENarangoaCribb2003&#95;191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENarangoaCribb2003-191"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Swami_Vivekananda" title="Swami Vivekananda">Swami Vivekananda</a>'s teachings on universalism, his nationalist thoughts and his emphasis on social service and reform had all inspired Subhas Chandra Bose from his very young days. The fresh interpretation of India's ancient scriptures had appealed immensely to him.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBoseWerthJogAyer1996&#95;192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoseWerthJogAyer1996-192"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some scholars think that Hindu spirituality formed an essential part of his political and social thought.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEChaudhuri1987&#95;193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaudhuri1987-193"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As historian Leonard Gordon explains "Inner religious explorations continued to be a part of his adult life. This set him apart from the slowly growing number of atheistic socialists and communists who dotted the Indian landscape."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990&#95;194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990-194"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Bose first expressed his preference for "a synthesis of what modern Europe calls <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascism</a>" in a 1930 speech in Calcutta.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEPasricha200864–65&#95;195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPasricha200864–65-195"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
Bose later criticised Nehru's 1933 statement that there is "no middle road" between <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communism</a> and fascism, describing it as "fundamentally wrong". Bose believed communism would not gain ground in India due to its rejection of nationalism and religion and suggested a "synthesis between communism and fascism" could take hold instead.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBose201198&#95;196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBose201198-196"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1944, Bose similarly stated, "Our philosophy should be a synthesis between <a href="/wiki/National_Socialism" class="mw-redirect" title="National Socialism">National Socialism</a> and communism."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEShanker&#95;Kapoor2017&#95;197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShanker_Kapoor2017-197"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Authoritarianism">Authoritarianism</h3></div>
<p>Bose believed that authoritarianism could bring liberation and reconstruction of Indian society.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He expressed admiration for the authoritarian methods which he saw in Italy and Germany during the 1930s; he thought they could be used to build an independent India.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTESen1999&#95;150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESen1999-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>To a large number of Congress leaders, Bose programme shared enough similarities with Japanese fascists.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEStein2010345&#95;199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein2010345-199"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After getting marginalised within Congress, Bose chose to embrace fascist regimes as allies against the British and fled India.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMetcalfMetcalf2012210&#95;20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMetcalfMetcalf2012210-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Louro-bose&#95;30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Louro-bose-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bose believed that India "must have a political system—State—of an authoritarian character," and "a strong central government with dictatorial powers for some years to come".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Earlier, Bose had clearly expressed his belief that democracy was the best option for India.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTERoy20047–8&#95;201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoy20047–8-201"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, during the war (and possibly as early as the 1930s), Bose seems to have decided that no democratic system could be adequate to overcome India's poverty and social inequalities, and he wrote that a socialist state similar to that of Soviet Russia (which he had also seen and admired) would be needed for the process of national re-building.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>aq<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Accordingly, some suggest that Bose's alliance with the Axis during the war was based on more than just pragmatism and that Bose was a militant nationalist, though not a Nazi nor a Fascist, for he supported the empowerment of women, secularism and other <a href="/wiki/Classical_liberalism" title="Classical liberalism">liberal</a> ideas; alternatively, others consider he might have been using populist methods of mobilisation common to many post-colonial leaders.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTESen1999&#95;150-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESen1999-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Antisemitism">Antisemitism</h3></div>
<p>Since before the beginning of World War II, Bose was opposed to the attempts to grant Jewish refugees asylum in India.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes2011165–166&#95;204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes2011165–166-204"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The great anti-Jewish pogrom called "<a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">the Night of Broken Glass</a>" happened on 9 November 1938. In early December, the pro-<a href="/wiki/Hindu_Mahasabha" title="Hindu Mahasabha">Hindu Mahasabha</a> journals published articles lending support to German anti-Semitism. This stance brought Hindu Mahasabha into conflict with the Congress which, on 12 December, issued a statement containing references to recent European events. Within the Congress, only Bose opposed this stance of the party. After some months in April 1939, Bose refused to support the party motion that Jews can find refuge in India.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTECasolari202089–90&#95;34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECasolari202089–90-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-combined-antisemetic&#95;206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-combined-antisemetic-206"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>167<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1938, Bose had denounced Nazi racial policy and persecution of Jews.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, in 1942 he had published an article in the journal <i>Angriff</i>, where he wrote that Indians were true Aryans and the 'brethren' of the Germans. Bose added that <a href="/wiki/Swastika" title="Swastika">Swastika</a> (symbol of Nazi Germany) was an ancient Indian symbol. Bose urged that anti-Semitism should be part of Indian liberation movement because the Jews assisted the British to exploit Indians.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jewish_Chronicle" title="The Jewish Chronicle">The Jewish Chronicle</a></i> had condemned Bose as "India's anti-Jewish <a href="/wiki/Quisling" title="Quisling">Quisling</a>" over this article.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>170<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Romain Hayes describes the troubled legacy of Bose with atrocities related to Jews in the following words:
</p>
<blockquote><p>The most troubling aspect of Bose's presence in Nazi Germany is not military or political but rather ethical. His alliance with the most genocidal regime in history poses serious dilemmas precisely because of his popularity and his having made a lifelong career of fighting the 'good cause'. How did a man who started his political career at the feet of <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Gandhi</a> end up with <a href="/wiki/Hitler" class="mw-redirect" title="Hitler">Hitler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mussolini" class="mw-redirect" title="Mussolini">Mussolini</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hideki_Tojo" title="Hideki Tojo">Tojo</a>? Even in the case of Mussolini and Tojo, the gravity of the dilemma pales in comparison to that posed by his association with Hitler and the Nazi leadership. The most disturbing issue, all too often ignored, is that in the many articles, minutes, memorandums, telegrams, letters, plans, and broadcasts Bose left behind in Germany, he did not express the slightest concern or sympathy for the millions who died in the concentration camps. Not one of his Berlin wartime associates or colleagues ever quotes him expressing any indignation. Not even when the horrors of Auschwitz and its satellite camps were exposed to the world upon being liberated by Soviet troops in early 1945, revealing publicly for the first time the genocidal nature of the Nazi regime, did Bose react.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes2011165&#95;96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes2011165-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Quotes">Quotes</h2></div>
<p>His most famous quote was "Give me blood and I will give you freedom".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKumar2010b&#95;214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKumar2010b-214"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Another famous quote was <i>Dilli Chalo</i> ("On to Delhi)!" This was the call he used to give the INA armies to motivate them. Another slogan coined by him was "Ittefaq, Etemad, Qurbani" (Urdu for "Unity, Agreement, Sacrifice").<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTERoy199651ff&#95;215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoy199651ff-215"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Legacy">Legacy</h2></div>
<p>Bose's defiance of British authority in India made him a hero among many Indians,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Mythic&#95;21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mythic-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>h<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>ar<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>as<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> however his wartime alliances with <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Imperial Japan</a> left a legacy fraught with authoritarianism, <a href="/wiki/Anti-Semitism" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Semitism">anti-Semitism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Military_incompetence" title="Military incompetence">military failure</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>at<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>173<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-combined-military-lead&#95;47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-combined-military-lead-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>au<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>av<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><br />
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Memorials">Memorials</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1273380762/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" /><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Subhas_Chandra_Bose_1964_stamp_of_India.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_1964_stamp_of_India.jpg/250px-Subhas_Chandra_Bose_1964_stamp_of_India.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_1964_stamp_of_India.jpg/330px-Subhas_Chandra_Bose_1964_stamp_of_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_1964_stamp_of_India.jpg/500px-Subhas_Chandra_Bose_1964_stamp_of_India.jpg 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="704" /></a></span></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Subhas_Chandra_Bose_1964_stamp_of_India_2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_1964_stamp_of_India_2.jpg/250px-Subhas_Chandra_Bose_1964_stamp_of_India_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="151" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_1964_stamp_of_India_2.jpg/330px-Subhas_Chandra_Bose_1964_stamp_of_India_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_1964_stamp_of_India_2.jpg/500px-Subhas_Chandra_Bose_1964_stamp_of_India_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="933" data-file-height="703" /></a></span></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Bose on 1964 stamps of India</div></div></div></div>
<p>Bose was featured on the stamps in India from 1964, 1993, 1997, 2001, 2016, 2018 and 2021.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>174<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bose was also featured in ₹2 coins in 1996 and 1997, ₹75 coin in 2018 and ₹125 coin in 2021.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>175<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>176<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>177<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Subhas_Chandra_Bose_International_Airport" title="Netaji Subhas Chandra Bose International Airport">Netaji Subhas Chandra Bose International Airport</a> at Kolkata, West Bengal; is named after him, as well as <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Subhas_Chandra_Bose_Gomoh_railway_station" title="Netaji Subhas Chandra Bose Gomoh railway station">Netaji Subhas Chandra Bose Gomoh railway station</a> at Gomoh, Jharkhand. <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Express" title="Netaji Express">Netaji Express</a>, a train runs between <a href="/wiki/Howrah_railway_station" title="Howrah railway station">Howrah</a>, West Bengal and <a href="/wiki/Kalka" title="Kalka">Kalka</a>, Haryana. <a href="/wiki/Cuttack_Netaji_Bus_Terminal" title="Cuttack Netaji Bus Terminal">Cuttack Netaji Bus Terminal</a> at Cuttack, Odisha. <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Bhavan_metro_station" title="Netaji Bhavan metro station">Netaji Bhavan metro station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Netaji_metro_station" title="Netaji metro station">Netaji metro station</a> at Kolkata, West Bengal and <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Subhash_Place_metro_station" title="Netaji Subhash Place metro station">Netaji Subhash Place metro station</a> at Delhi. <a href="/wiki/Ross_Island,_South_Andaman_district" title="Ross Island, South Andaman district">Netaji Subhash Chandra Bose Island</a> at Andaman and Nicobar Island. <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Subhas_Chandra_Bose_Setu" title="Netaji Subhas Chandra Bose Setu">Netaji Subhas Chandra Bose Setu</a> (Longest bridge of Odisha) at Cuttack, Odisha. <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Subhash_Chandra_Bose_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="Netaji Subhash Chandra Bose Road">Netaji Subhash Chandra Bose Road</a> at Kolkata, West Bengal. <a href="/wiki/INA_War_Museum" title="INA War Museum">INA War Museum</a> at Moirang, Manipur. <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Indoor_Stadium" title="Netaji Indoor Stadium">Netaji Indoor Stadium</a> at Kolkata, West Bengal, <a href="/wiki/DDA_Netaji_Subhash_Sports_Complex" title="DDA Netaji Subhash Sports Complex">DDA Netaji Subhash Sports Complex</a> at Delhi, <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Stadium" title="Netaji Stadium">Netaji Stadium</a> at Port Blair, Andaman and Nicobar Island. <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Subhas_Open_University" title="Netaji Subhas Open University">Netaji Subhas Open University</a> at Kolkata, West Bengal, <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Subhash_University_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Netaji Subhash University of Technology">Netaji Subhash University of Technology</a> at Delhi, <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Subhas_University" title="Netaji Subhas University">Netaji Subhas University</a> at Jamshedpur, Jharkhand and many other things in India are named after him. On 23 August 2007, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Prime Minister">Japanese Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shinz%C5%8D_Abe" class="mw-redirect" title="Shinzō Abe">Shinzō Abe</a> visited the <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Bhawan" title="Netaji Bhawan">Netaji Bhawan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTERoche2007&#95;226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoche2007-226"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>178<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEThe&#95;Hindu2007&#95;227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Hindu2007-227"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>179<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Abe, who is also the recipient of Netaji Award 2022,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>180<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> said to Bose's family "The Japanese are deeply moved by Bose's strong will to have led the <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">Indian independence movement</a> from British rule. Netaji is a much respected name in Japan."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTERoche2007&#95;226-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoche2007-226"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>178<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEThe&#95;Hindu2007&#95;227-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Hindu2007-227"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>179<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2021, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a> declared 23 January as <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Jayanti" title="Netaji Jayanti">Parakram Divas</a> to commemorate the birth anniversary of Subhas Chandra Bose. Political party, <a href="/wiki/Trinamool_Congress" title="Trinamool Congress">Trinamool Congress</a> and the <a href="/wiki/All_India_Forward_Bloc" title="All India Forward Bloc">All India Forward Bloc</a> demanded that the day should be observed as 'Deshprem Divas'.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>181<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2019, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a> inaugurated a museum on Netaji Subhash Chandra Bose and his INA at <a href="/wiki/Red_Fort" title="Red Fort">Red Fort</a>, New Delhi. In 2022, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a> inaugurated a Statue of <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Subhas_Chandra_Bose" title="Statue of Subhas Chandra Bose">Netaji Subhas Chandra Bose</a> at <a href="/wiki/India_Gate" title="India Gate">India Gate</a>. Also in the same year, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a> started an official award <a href="/wiki/Subhas_Chandra_Bose_Aapda_Prabandhan_Puraskar" class="mw-redirect" title="Subhas Chandra Bose Aapda Prabandhan Puraskar">Subhas Chandra Bose Aapda Prabandhan Puraskar</a>, for those who do excellent work in disaster management.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>182<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>183<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="In_popular_media">In popular media</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:The_tableau_of_Andaman_%26_Nicobar_depicting_the_%27100_years_of_Cellular_Jail_%27,_passes_through_the_Rajpath_during_the_Republic_Day_Parade_-_2006,_in_New_Delhi_on_January_26,_2006.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/The_tableau_of_Andaman_%26_Nicobar_depicting_the_%27100_years_of_Cellular_Jail_%27%2C_passes_through_the_Rajpath_during_the_Republic_Day_Parade_-_2006%2C_in_New_Delhi_on_January_26%2C_2006.jpg/250px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/The_tableau_of_Andaman_%26_Nicobar_depicting_the_%27100_years_of_Cellular_Jail_%27%2C_passes_through_the_Rajpath_during_the_Republic_Day_Parade_-_2006%2C_in_New_Delhi_on_January_26%2C_2006.jpg/500px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="728" /></a><figcaption>Bose on the tableau of Andaman &amp; Nicobar in the 2006 <a href="/wiki/Republic_Day_Parade" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic Day Parade">Republic Day Parade</a> in New Delhi</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Netaji_Subhas_Chandra_Bose.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Netaji_Subhas_Chandra_Bose.jpg/250px-Netaji_Subhas_Chandra_Bose.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="342" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7e/Netaji_Subhas_Chandra_Bose.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="263" data-file-height="360" /></a><figcaption>Subhas in Army uniform</figcaption></figure>
<ul><li><i>Netaji Subhash</i>, a feature documentary film about Bose was released in 1947, it was directed by Chhotubhai Desai.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-film&#95;232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-film-232"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>184<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Subhas_Chandra" title="Subhas Chandra">Subhas Chandra</a></i> is a 1966 Indian <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a>-language biographical film, directed by Pijush Basu.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>185<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEDas&#95;Gupta2015&#95;234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDas_Gupta2015-234"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>186<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i>Neta Ji Subhash Chandra Bose</i> is a 1966 Indian biographical drama film about Bose by <a href="/wiki/Hemen_Gupta" title="Hemen Gupta">Hemen Gupta</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-film&#95;232-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-film-232"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>184<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Shyam_Benegal" title="Shyam Benegal">Shyam Benegal</a> directed the biographical film, <i><a href="/wiki/Netaji_Subhas_Chandra_Bose:_The_Forgotten_Hero" title="Netaji Subhas Chandra Bose: The Forgotten Hero">Netaji Subhas Chandra Bose: The Forgotten Hero</a></i> depicting his life in <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> (1941–1943), in Japanese-occupied Asia (1943–1945) and the events leading to the formation of <a href="/wiki/Azad_Hind_Fauj" class="mw-redirect" title="Azad Hind Fauj">Azad Hind Fauj</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTESalam2005&#95;235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESalam2005-235"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>187<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The film received critical acclaim at the <a href="/wiki/BFI_London_Film_Festival" title="BFI London Film Festival">BFI London Film Festival</a>, and has garnered the <a href="/wiki/Nargis_Dutt_Award_for_Best_Feature_Film_on_National_Integration" title="Nargis Dutt Award for Best Feature Film on National Integration">National Film Award for Best Feature Film on National Integration</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Award_for_Best_Art_Direction" class="mw-redirect" title="National Film Award for Best Art Direction">National Film Award for Best Production Design</a> for that year.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEPandohar2005&#95;236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPandohar2005-236"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>188<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEThe&#95;Guardian2005&#95;237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Guardian2005-237"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>189<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mahanayak_(novel)" title="Mahanayak (novel)">Mahanayak</a>, 2005 published <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a> historical novel on the life of Subhash Chandra Bose, written by Marathi author <a href="/wiki/Vishvas_Patil" class="mw-redirect" title="Vishvas Patil">Vishvas Patil</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/His_Majesty%27s_Opponent" title="His Majesty&#39;s Opponent">His Majesty's Opponent</a></i>, a biography of Subhash Chandra Bose, written by <a href="/wiki/Sugata_Bose" title="Sugata Bose">Sugata Bose</a>, published in 2011.</li>
<li><i>Subhash Chandra Bose: The Mystery</i>, a 2016 documentary film by Iqbal Malhotra, follows conspiracy theories regarding Bose's death.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>190<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i>Netaji Bose – The Lost Treasure</i> is a 2017 television documentary film which aired on <a href="/wiki/History_TV18" title="History TV18">History TV18</a>, it explores the <a href="/wiki/INA_treasure_controversy" title="INA treasure controversy">INA treasure controversy</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-HistoryTV18&#95;239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistoryTV18-239"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>191<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2017, <a href="/wiki/ALTBalaji" class="mw-redirect" title="ALTBalaji">ALTBalaji</a> and BIG Synergy Media, released a 9-episode web series, <a href="/wiki/Bose:_Dead/Alive" title="Bose: Dead/Alive">Bose: Dead/Alive</a>, created by <a href="/wiki/Ekta_Kapoor" title="Ekta Kapoor">Ekta Kapoor</a>, a dramatised version of the book <i>India's Biggest Cover-up</i> written by <a href="/wiki/Anuj_Dhar" title="Anuj Dhar">Anuj Dhar</a>, which starred <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" class="mw-redirect" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> actor <a href="/wiki/Rajkummar_Rao" title="Rajkummar Rao">Rajkummar Rao</a> as Subhas Chandra Bose and Anna Ador as <a href="/wiki/Emilie_Schenkl" title="Emilie Schenkl">Emilie Schenkl</a>. The series was praised by both audience and critics, for its plot, performance and production design.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGauri2017&#95;240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGauri2017-240"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>192<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In January 2019 <a href="/wiki/Zee_Bangla" title="Zee Bangla">Zee Bangla</a> started broadcasting the daily television series <i><a href="/wiki/Netaji_(TV_series)" title="Netaji (TV series)">Netaji</a></i>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Gumnaami" title="Gumnaami">Gumnaami</a></i> is a 2019 Indian <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a> <a href="/wiki/Mystery_film" title="Mystery film">mystery film</a> directed by <a href="/wiki/Srijit_Mukherji" title="Srijit Mukherji">Srijit Mukherji</a>, which deals with Netaji's death mystery, based on the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Subhas_Chandra_Bose#Mukherjee_Commission_2005" title="Death of Subhas Chandra Bose">Mukherjee Commission Hearings</a>.</li></ul>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1327269900">.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}body.skin-vector-2022 .mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:27em}body.skin-vector-2022 .mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:22.5em}.mw-parser-output .references[data-mw-group=upper-alpha]{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .references[data-mw-group=upper-roman]{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .references[data-mw-group=lower-alpha]{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .references[data-mw-group=lower-greek]{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .references[data-mw-group=lower-roman]{list-style-type:lower-roman}.mw-parser-output div.reflist-liststyle-upper-alpha .references{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output div.reflist-liststyle-upper-roman .references{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output div.reflist-liststyle-lower-alpha .references{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output div.reflist-liststyle-lower-greek .references{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output div.reflist-liststyle-lower-roman .references{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns" style="column-width: calc( 0.9 * 40em );"><ol class="references" data-mw-group="lower-alpha">
<li id="cite&#95;note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"The Japanese navy was unwilling to transfer administration of [the Andaman and Nicobar Islands] to Bose's forces, but a face-saving agreement was worked out so that the provisional government was given a 'jurisdiction', while actual control remained throughout with the Japanese military... Bose continued to lobby for complete transfer, but did not succeed."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990502–503&#95;3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990502–503-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">His formal title after 21 October 1943 was: Head of State, Prime Minister, Minister of War, and Minister of Foreign Affairs of the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Government_of_Free_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Provisional Government of Free India">Provisional Government of Free India</a>, which was based in <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_Singapore" title="Japanese occupation of Singapore">Japanese-occupied Singapore</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon1990502&#95;1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon1990502-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEWolpert2000339&#95;2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolpert2000339-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> with jurisdiction but not sovereignty over <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_the_Andaman_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese occupation of the Andaman Islands">Japanese-occupied Andaman Islands</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>a<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Secretly married without ceremony or witnesses, unacknowledged publicly by Bose.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEHayes201115&#95;8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayes201115-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Expelled from the college and rusticated from the university, 15 February 1916;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199048&#95;12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199048-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> reinstated in the university 20 July 1917.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199052&#95;13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199052-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"When another run-in between Professor Oaten and some students took place on February 15 (1916), a group of students including Subhas Bose, ... decided to take the law in their own hands. Coming down the broad staircase from the second floor, Oaten was surrounded (the) students who beat him with their sandals—and fled. Although Oaten himself was not able to identify any of the attackers, a bearer said he saw Subhas Bose and Ananga Dam among those fleeing. Rumors in student circles also placed Subhas among the group. An investigation was carried out by the college authorities, and these two were expelled from the college and rusticated from the university.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGordon199048&#95;12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon199048-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Upon arriving in Britain, Bose went up to Cambridge to gain admission. He managed to gain entry to Fitzwilliam Hall, a body for non-collegiate members of the University. Bose took the Mental and Moral Sciences Tripos."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Bengali:</span> <span class="IPA
