<li id="cite&#95;note-198"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-198">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><cite id="CITEREFDeka2013" class="citation cs2">Deka, Meeta (2013), <i>Women's Agency and Social Change: Assam and Beyond</i>, SAGE Studies on India's North East, New Delhi and Thousand Oaks, CA: SAGE Publications, <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-81-321-1138-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-81-321-1138-2"><bdi>978-81-321-1138-2</bdi></a>, <q>(pp. 134–135) Bose was convinced that his ideology could bring about the liberation of India and a total reconstruction of Indian society along authoritarian-socialist lines, envisaging gender equality therein. As mayor of Calcutta, he believed that his policy and programme was a synthesis of socialism and fascism, on the lines of modern Europe. In the early 1930s, he stated, 'We have here the justice, the equality, the love, which is the basis of Socialism as it stands in Europe today.' In the late 1930s, he reiterated his belief in the efficacy of authoritarian government and a synthesis of fascism and socialism, while in 1944 when addressing the students at Tokyo University, he asserted that India must have a political system 'of an authoritarian character ... [and] our philosophy should be a synthesis between National Socialism and Communism'.</q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Women%27s+Agency+and+Social+Change%3A+Assam+and+Beyond&amp;rft.place=New+Delhi+and+Thousand+Oaks%2C+CA&amp;rft.series=SAGE+Studies+on+India%27s+North+East&amp;rft.pub=SAGE+Publications&amp;rft.date=2013&amp;rft.isbn=978-81-321-1138-2&amp;rft.aulast=Deka&amp;rft.aufirst=Meeta&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASubhas+Chandra+Bose" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-FOOTNOTEStein2010345-199"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein2010345_199-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFStein2010">Stein 2010</a>, pp.&#160;345.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-200"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-200">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><cite id="CITEREFHarrison1960" class="citation cs2">Harrison, Selig S. (1960), <i>India: The Most Dangerous Decades</i>, Princeton Legacy Library, Princeton, NJ: Princeton University Press, p.&#160;314, <a href="/wiki/LCCN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="LCCN (identifier)">LCCN</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://lccn.loc.gov/60005749">60005749</a>, <q>The most categorical and unabashed program for dictatorship in India's political heritage, finally, was laid down by the late Subhas Chandra Bose. He argued that India "must have a political system—State—of an authoritarian character," "a strong central government with dictatorial powers for some years to come," "a government by a strong party bound together by military discipline ... as the only means of holding India together." The next phase in world history, Bose predicted, would produce "a synthesis between Communism and Fascism, and will it be a surprise if that synthesis is produced in India?"<span class="cs1-kern-right"></span></q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=India%3A+The+Most+Dangerous+Decades&amp;rft.place=Princeton%2C+NJ&amp;rft.series=Princeton+Legacy+Library&amp;rft.pages=314&amp;rft.pub=Princeton+University+Press&amp;rft.date=1960&amp;rft&#95;id=info%3Alccn%2F60005749&amp;rft.aulast=Harrison&amp;rft.aufirst=Selig+S.&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASubhas+Chandra+Bose" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-FOOTNOTERoy20047–8-201"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoy20047–8_201-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFRoy2004">Roy 2004</a>, pp.&#160;7–8.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-FOOTNOTEBoseBose1997a319–320-202"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoseBose1997a319–320_202-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFBoseBose1997a">Bose &amp; Bose 1997a</a>, pp.&#160;319–320.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-FOOTNOTEHayes2011165–166-204"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHayes2011165–166_204-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFHayes2011">Hayes 2011</a>, pp.&#160;165–166.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-205"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-205">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><cite id="CITEREFKumaraswamy2020" class="citation cs2">Kumaraswamy, P. R. (2020), <i>Squaring the Circle: Mahatma Gandhi and the Jewish National Home</i>, Routledge, p.&#160;153, <q>In his presidential address, Subhas Chandra Bose highlighted the contradictory nature of the British Empire and its inconsistent policy over Palestine. As a heterogeneous empire, Bose observed, the British had to be pro-Arab in India and pro Jewish elsewhere, and accused that London "has to please Jews because she cannot ignore Jewish high finance. On the other hand, the India Office and Foreign Office have to placate the Arabs because of the Imperial interests in the Near East and India."' While his reasoning was logical, Bose's anti-Jewish slur was no different from the anti-Semitic remarks in the (Muslim) League deliberations referred to earlier. Bose also opposed Nehru's efforts to provide asylum to a limited number of European Jewish refugees who were fleeing from Nazi persecution. Despite the opposition led by Bose, Nehru "was a strong supporter of inviting (Jewish refugees) to settle down in India... (and felt that) this was the only way by which Jews could be saved from the wrath of the Nazis... Between 1933 and the outbreak of the War, Nehru was instrumental in obtaining the entry of several German Jewish refugees into India"<span class="cs1-kern-right"></span></q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Squaring+the+Circle%3A+Mahatma+Gandhi+and+the+Jewish+National+Home&amp;rft.pages=153&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2020&amp;rft.aulast=Kumaraswamy&amp;rft.aufirst=P.+R.&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASubhas+Chandra+Bose" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-combined-antisemetic-206"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-combined-antisemetic_206-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><cite id="CITEREFBruckenhaus2017" class="citation cs2">Bruckenhaus, Daniel (2017), <i>Policing Transnational Protest: Liberal Imperialism and the Surveillance of Anticolonialists in Europe, 1905–1945</i>, Oxford: Oxford University Press, p.&#160;213, <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-066001-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-066001-7"><bdi>978-0-19-066001-7</bdi></a>, <a href="/wiki/LCCN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="LCCN (identifier)">LCCN</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://lccn.loc.gov/2016042217">2016042217</a>, <q>Epilogue and conclusion: Finally, however, the example of Germany also demonstrates that their work in Europe frequently forced anticolonialists to make difficult moral choices, as their presence in that continent required them to take a position not only on colonialism worldwide, but also on inner-European political and ideological conflicts. This was true, especially, during World War II. The war situation brought to stark light, one last time, the contradictions within the western political model of rule, leading to a rift among the anticolonialists then present in Europe. As the western empires fought against Nazi Germany, most anticolonialists felt that they could no longer support, simultaneously, the emancipatory projects of anticolonialism and antifascism. Some, such as Subhas Chandra Bose, began to cooperate with the radically racist Nazis against colonialism, while others decided to work against Nazism with the very western authorities who had been engaged, over the previous decades, in creating a widespread network of trans-national surveillance against them.</q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Policing+Transnational+Protest%3A+Liberal+Imperialism+and+the+Surveillance+of+Anticolonialists+in+Europe%2C+1905%E2%80%931945&amp;rft.place=Oxford&amp;rft.pages=213&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2017&amp;rft&#95;id=info%3Alccn%2F2016042217&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-19-066001-7&amp;rft.aulast=Bruckenhaus&amp;rft.aufirst=Daniel&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASubhas+Chandra+Bose" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-207"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-207">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><cite id="CITEREFRoland2017" class="citation cs2">Roland, Joan G. (2017), <i>Jewish Communities in India: Identity in a Colonial Era</i>, Routledge, p.&#160;342, <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-7658-0439-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-7658-0439-6"><bdi>978-0-7658-0439-6</bdi></a>, <q>On 21 August 1942 the Jewish Chronicle of London reported that Bose was anti-Semitic and had published an article in Angriff, the organ of Goebbels, in which he described Indians as the real ancient Aryans and the brethren of the German people. He had said that the swastika was an old Indian sign and that anti-Semitism must become a part of the Indian freedom movement, since the Jews, he alleged, had helped Britain to exploit and oppress the Indians. The Jewish Advocate expressed horror at Bose's statement about a Jewish role in India's exploitation but added, "one may expect anything from one who has traveled the road to Berlin in search of his country's salvation." Norman Shohet pointed out how insignificant a part in the economic and political life of the country the Jews of India actually played. He also mentioned that other Indian leaders had so far not shown any anti-Semitic leanings, but that on the contrary, Gandhi, Nehru, Dr. B. R. Ambedkar, and others had been positively friendly to the Jews.</q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Jewish+Communities+in+India%3A+Identity+in+a+Colonial+Era&amp;rft.pages=342&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2017&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-7658-0439-6&amp;rft.aulast=Roland&amp;rft.aufirst=Joan+G.&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASubhas+Chandra+Bose" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-208"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-208">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><cite id="CITEREFAafreedi2021" class="citation cs2">Aafreedi, Navras J. (2021), "Holocaust education in India and its challenges", in Aafreedi, Navras J.; Singh, Priya (eds.), <i>Conceptualizing Mass Violence: Representations, Recollections, and reinterpretatons</i>, Abington and New York: Routledge, p.&#160;154, <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-00-314613-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-00-314613-1"><bdi>978-1-00-314613-1</bdi></a>, <q>Jawaharlal Nehru called the Jews 'People without a home or nation' and sponsored a resolution in the Congress Working Committee. Although the exact date is not known, yet it can be said that it probably happened in December 1938 at the Wardha session, the one that took place shortly after Nehru returned from Europe. The draft resolution read: 'The Committee sees no objection to the employment in India of such Jewish refugees as are experts and specialists and who can fit in with the new order in India and accept Indian standards.' It was, however, rejected by the then Congress President Subhas Chandra Bose, who four years later in 1942 was reported by the <i>Jewish Chronicle</i> of London as having published an article in <i>Angriff</i>, a journal of Goebbels, saying that "anti-Semitism should become part of the Indian liberation movement because Jews had helped the British to exploit Indians (21 August 1942)" Although by then Bose had left the Congress, he continued to command a strong influence within the party.</q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Holocaust+education+in+India+and+its+challenges&amp;rft.btitle=Conceptualizing+Mass+Violence%3A+Representations%2C+Recollections%2C+and+reinterpretatons&amp;rft.place=Abington+and+New+York&amp;rft.pages=154&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2021&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-00-314613-1&amp;rft.aulast=Aafreedi&amp;rft.aufirst=Navras+J.&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASubhas+Chandra+Bose" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-209"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-209">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><cite id="CITEREFWeinberg2011" class="citation cs2">Weinberg, Gerhard L. (2011), <i>A World at Arms: A Global History of World War II</i>, Cambridge and New York: Cambridge University Press, 2nd Edition, p.&#160;xx, <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-521-61826-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-521-61826-7"><bdi>978-0-521-61826-7</bdi></a>, <q>None of the works that deal with ... Subhas Chandra Bose, or his Indian National Army has engaged either Bose's reaction to German mass killing of Sinti and Roma (Gypsies) because their ancestors came from India or the reaction of the soldiers in his army to the sex slaves kidnapped in Japanese-occupied lands and held in enclosures attached to the camps in which they were being trained to follow their Japanese comrades in the occupation of India.</q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+World+at+Arms%3A+A+Global+History+of+World+War+II&amp;rft.place=Cambridge+and+New+York&amp;rft.pages=xx&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press%2C+2nd+Edition&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-521-61826-7&amp;rft.aulast=Weinberg&amp;rft.aufirst=Gerhard+L.&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASubhas+Chandra+Bose" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-210"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-210">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><cite id="CITEREFShindler2010" class="citation cs2">Shindler, Colin (2010), <i>Israel and the European Left: Between Solidarity and Deligitimization</i>, New York: Bloomsbury Publishing, Continuum, p.&#160;112, <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4411-8898-4" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-4411-8898-4"><bdi>978-1-4411-8898-4</bdi></a>, <q>Bose requested a declaration from the Germans that they supported the movement for freedom in India—and in Arab countries. He had opposed Nehru in permitting political asylum to Jews fleeing Europe in 1939. He was prepared to ingratiate himself with Nazi ideology by writing for Goebells's <i>Der Angriff</i> in 1942. He argued that anti-Semitism should become a factor in the struggle for Indian freedom since the Jews had collaborated with British imperialism to exploit the country and its inhabitants.</q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Israel+and+the+European+Left%3A+Between+Solidarity+and+Deligitimization&amp;rft.place=New+York&amp;rft.pages=112&amp;rft.pub=Bloomsbury+Publishing%2C+Continuum&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4411-8898-4&amp;rft.aulast=Shindler&amp;rft.aufirst=Colin&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASubhas+Chandra+Bose" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-211"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-211">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Bose to Dr. Thierfelder of the <i>Deutsche Academie</i>, Kurhaus Hochland, Badgastein, 25 March 1936 <a href="#CITEREFBoseBose1997a">Bose &amp; Bose 1997a</a>, p.&#160;155</span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-212"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-212">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><cite id="CITEREFEgorova2008" class="citation book cs1">Egorova, Yulia (2008). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=1m_okSx7ds4C"><i>Jews and India: Perceptions and Image</i></a>. <li id="cite&#95;note-213"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-213">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><cite id="CITEREFNoorani2012" class="citation news cs1">Noorani, A.G. <li id="cite&#95;note-219"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-219">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"At the same time that the Japanese appreciated the firmness with which Bose's forces continued to fight, they were endlessly exasperated with him.
